RATING: 8.6
I love the idea of this game- Eldritch Horror Lite with lots of dice rolling- what can be bad? But the pieces are tiny and fiddly, the characters are literally smaller than dimes. As a tactile or visual experience, the game fails but I guess gets points for portability. Must be played with Gates of Arkham expansion unless playing with children or new gamers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Fun coop game (if you can bear a lot of dice rolls, and the resulting randomness), which I usually play solo (with 2 characters).
There's quite a lot of randomness, but you still have to choose well to have a chance of winning the game.
I very much like Lovecraft's work, and in this game the theme is well represented (obviously not as much as in larger games like eldritch/arkham horror, but it is quite enjoyable). You obviously have to get over the fact that you are going around throwing explosive and shooting around, which is something never found in any of Lovecraft's works.

This game really shines with the gates of arkham expansion, adding some more theme and difficulty (which is needed after some games), together with some interesting new mechanics. GoA is the last expansion published in Italy, so I haven't tried omens of ice yet (but it looks great!)

The main negative aspect is that the setup/tear down is very boring (not particularly long, but you have to shuffle something like 10 decks of cards). I'd say that a custom inserted (I made one like this https://boardgamegeek.com/geeklist/115468/item/3814058#item3814058) is necessary to avoid having to use a lot of ziplocks to divide everything.

Relative to Arkham and Eldritch, this game is the most approachable, and the 90-minute playtime makes it more versatile. I particularly appreciate how well-integrated the theme is. This game would have scored even higher if this game had more actual cooperation (players helping each other) as opposed to merely players trying to achieve the same objective and (at best) providing healing.

RATING: 5.9
The good:
-fun theme
-Exciting to do the tasks knowing what you're risking and the possible reward and it all hinges on your dice rolls. It makes the individual task fun.

The bad:
-It's basically co-op without cooperation. There aren't any meaningful mechanics to allow you work together. Sure you can deliberate about what to do, but even that hasn't meant much since...
-Choices are easy. It's pretty no-brainer what you need to do and which tasks to go for.
-The game itself is too easy. Co-ops should be more tense and you actually feel like you might lose.

The only reason I'm trading it away is that it is better as an app than a board game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
A better game than the rating, but for some mysterious reason, I have horrific dice luck in these type of games, and no matter how solid a design, when it all goes bad -- REALLY bad -- it will take away from your enjoyment level, and my dice luck in these type of horror games is statistically, nay, supernaturally bad.

I probably enjoyed it more than Arkham Horror (AH), but that is because when your luck is horrific, you'd just as soon not have the game drag out when you know you are going to lose.  However, if you are a big Arkham Horror fan, and want a dice game that captures theme but in a short, quick format, I don't think this is going to scratch your itch.  You don't get the feel for solving a mystery or fighting monsters, but rather rolling dice and matching symbols.  Not that this is bad thing, but I'm guessing AH fans are in it for the story more than the mechanics.

It isn't as close to the original game than, say, [thing=12]Ra's[/thing] dice [thing=35503] variant [/thing] is to it, but that's because Ra is a Euro and has no theme, so the dice do not take away from a non-existent story.  So if I liked this more, why did I rate it lower?  Because if I were to experience a "normal" game of each (where my dice luck isn't supernaturally bad), I would like the original better and wouldn't mind the length of the game.

RATING: 7
FAVOURITE GAME - This is a quite nice, and fast-paced cooperative game, where you have to fulfill different tasks by rolling dice for different locations represented by cards. It is very luck based, but by acquiring weapons, skills and magical abilities you can somewhat mitigate it. It plays extremly well in 2-player mode, with more players you have to be very careful how you plan and use your abilities as the Ancient One can awake very quickly. And yes, this game is also based on the Lovecraftian universe. It has a huge replayability thanks to the many cards it provides.

RATING: 4
An attempt to condense Arkham Horror into a small box package playable in an hour.  Sadly, in the process much of the mythos flavour is lost. I never felt as though I was solving mysteries or battling horrors; I was just rolling combinations of dice.  And, really, who wants to play Yahtzee for an hour or more?

What's more, as others have commented, Elder Sign seems too easy.  The name of the game is a big clue as to what you need to do - collect elder signs.  Even when we failed to take that hint in our first game, four of us still managed to down Nyarlathotep in a final confrontation.

Artwork and production quality are up to Fantasy Flight's usual good standards.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I am a sucker for the FF Arkham Files, and the idea of a quick & dirty Arkham experience drew me to Elder Sign.

As anyone who has played Arkham Horror/Eldritch Horror knows it takes a special game group to get these babies on the table, with a large # of components and pieces which can intimate new players and the time required can be a turn off.

Elder Signs proposes a solution to this issue and for the most part succeeds. At it's core Elder Signs is a Dice Rolling game, while it shares Theme, Art, Setting and overall feel with the rest of the Arkham File series the base game feels like a lighter game which works to both its benefit & detriment.

Pros: 
Short set up time.
Art/Theme is in line with the Cthulu charm from other Arkham titles (although flavour text is not as involved)
Faster play time, I can see this being an easier sell to most groups as it is all around the fastest in the series.
You get to roll dice which is fun.
Simple and easy to learn, far more streamlined then other Akrham File games
Simple Iconography

Cons:
THE DICE ARE HIDEOUS. In a dice game, I expect to have some decent dice. While Elder Signs dice seem well constructed their design & iconography fit the universe the dice themselves are bright vibrant primary colour green, yellow & red which frankly look awful next to the well designed cards, investigators and everything else.

Investigator Tokens are tiny and will get lost. Also they are hard to see. Honestly, I am likely going to use my Arkham/Eldritch investigators in future play throughs.

Some of the theme/variability is lost in the smaller box. There are very few items/spells in the base game (getting an expansion greatly aids this issue) and most of their abilities are similar to one another. 

All in all Elder Signs is a much more Task Focused game in the series, but its faster set up & play time makes it a great intro game to the Arkham Files and one you will likely play more often. 

But please someone, for the love of god, make some custom dice for this (I am working on it, but my design skills are terrible).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
This is pretty fiddly – there are some extremely small counters and the monster tokens are too tiny to really convey what they're about. In fact, I don't think the game succeeds in conveying much flavour at all. It's got a horror theme but you're never likely to get a hint of dread. Everything is focused on the game mechanics, which are perfectly fine if not very original. You weigh-up the rolls needed to tackle a task, factor in any cards you possess that could influence your chances, consider whether the potential rewards are worth the potential penalties and then either go ahead or back down. I'm not saying it's dull, but it's only as exciting as an abstract dice game.

RATING: 8
Számomra ez egy kalandozás a "másfajta" (nem eurogame) játékok világába.
Mit is mondhatnék? - remek ötlet volt a kitérő ezen remek játékhoz...!
Rengeteg a kockadobás, de mégsem mondanám szerencsejátéknak. Sok mindenre figyelemmel kell lenni a teljesítendő kalandlapok kiválasztásakor, és azok teljesítésekor.
Igazán izgalmas a játékmenet - bár a szabályok egyszerűnek tűnnek, mégis több helyen pontosításokat igényel(né)nek. (111225 - 16 oldalnyi kérdés a játékkal kapcsolatosan  - túl sok!)

A játék kivitelezése méltó az FFG kiadásokhoz, igazán öröm vele játszani.
További előny az "egyjátékos" játék módozat, továbbá a játékidő hossza.
Annyira tematikusnak érzem, hogy játék közben szinte látom magam előtt a játékból készítendő filmet.
Hátrány - az óra, dobozban történő elhelyezésének megoldatlansága. (a tároló rekesz kismértékű átalakításával azonban ez a "hiba" korrigálható)

"Bármikor" kategória, és úgy vélem kezdőkkel is nagyszerűn játszható...
Az egyik legjobb, ha nem a legjobb kooperatív játék - amivel eddig játszottam.

RATING: 8.5
FAVORITE MEDIUM WEIGHT COOPERATIVE GAME RUNNER-UP

1-8 Players (Best: 4) / 90 Min / Weight: 2.35
Type: Thematic / Co-op / Solo

Expansions Owned:

Elder Sign: Unseen Forces
Elder Sign: Gates of Arkham

Rating is based on Base + Unseen Forces Expansion.

I've played Elder Sign: Omen a lot before I got physical version of the game. Since I got the physical version, I've played solo once so far (using Unseen Forces expansion). I like it as much as I like Elder Sign: Omen.

At first this game looked like just a dicefest luck based game, and I thought this is impossible to win without being extremely lucky. However, after a few play and reading some strategy advice, I found that this is all about luck management. It is very important to utilize all the resources - items and special abilities - to manage the luck.

I used to dislike push-your-luck games, but after playing this, I started liking push-your-luck mechanic based on dice rolling. I still don't like push-your-luck games based on card much.

I am so expecting to get Gate of Arkham expansion.

RATING: 7.4
Arkham Horror express! That's what this is. They attempted to distil all the theme and awesomeness of Arkham Horror into a simple dice matching mechanic. Naturally a lot of the theme got lost and therefore it certainly won't replace Arkham in my house. But the pro's of this game are also substantial. The quick setup time and much shorter playing time will mean it hits the table more. It also means this, as opposed to AH, is actually a viable solo game. Components are great and the rulebook is not as horrible as an average FF rulebook. Enough of the theme remains and the game is meaty enough for me to like it as a quick solo game.

Gameplay: :star::star::star::halfstar::nostar:
Replayability: :star::star::star::halfstar::nostar:
Fun/Social: :star::star::star::star::nostar:
Components: :star::star::star::star::halfstar:
Rules: :star::star::star::halfstar::nostar:
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Decent enough game.  I think it really comes down to playing up the theme as much as possible. 

It can be easy to fall into the mode of looking at what "symbols" you need and rolling to get them, which is when this game is at it's worst and doesn't seem like a very compelling game.  

It really helps to play this with a few people who like to come-up with "logical" reasons, for example, for the likes of Harrigan to be running around on the ledge of a building (adventure description) which he uses a bullwhip (add the yellow die) to succeed, which spins off into "Oh it's just Harrigan, he's just a mashup of Homer Simpson and your favorite anti-hero."

All in all, a game who's appeal can fluctuate especially wide depending on the groups willingness try to come up with reasons for their characters to be doing such off-the-wall things to combat the awakening of the elder god.

RATING: 7
I'm rating this only as a solo game. I don't see enough interesting decisions to promote discussion with more than one. Perhaps it might be nice for two.

Elder Sign is a strange bird. It's a nice, elegant litle game, a fact which is a bit incongruent with it's theme of cosmic awfulness. Oddly, the theme seems to carry it, though. This, too (!) is strange as I'll give the game credit for generating theme during a solo session, which is not easy for a solitaire game to do.

Ultimately, I can't rate this above a seven because almost always the right move becomes apparent after a moment's thought. There is some risk/reward with the dice for taking longshots, but there really seems to be a basement of mechanical depth. It is both easy to win and, more to the point, easy to know how to win. I do think I'll find myself playing and looking forward to playing it when I'm in the mood for a light solo game. I just can't rate it high enough to stand with Space Hulk or other games which pack more into the experience.

RATING: 3
I was expecting Arkham Horror express ... what I saw wasn't quite that :(

Monsters appear, challenges appear, you can sometimes get a gate, there's a GOO to defeat. So it all sounded good, you get a unique character with mind and health, and items, spells.

But when playing a big chunk of the flavour is lost, there is no real sense of narrative for me - and the decisions are rather trivial, I certainly didn't feel I was exploring, avoiding monsters, fighting monsters in a thankless role trying to beat back the nameless dread. Probably my hopes and expectations were unrealistic.

If this played in 20 minutes it would be fine, but it takes about an hour, and the process of streamlining this far has removed the flavour leaving a yahtzee variant that takes an hour, I'd have prefered they went further and made the game quicker. 

But I love the setting, so I could put up with that adding the flavour by reading out loud the diary text etc, but it's far too easy - first game with none of us sure what we were doing we got the required elder signs in about 6 'days' - with no deaths. All rather disapointing.

Production is top notch, reused art from the the CCG/LCG, cool dice - but game left me stone cold and running screaming, for all the wrong reasons.

RATING: 7
Quoted from forums:


Variant to try:

"It's very simple to implement, and makes for challenging games.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
The following components are used


Components from Gates of Arkham: 

The Streets of Arkham Entrance sheet
Event cards
gate tokens
seal tokens
Skill cards(combined with those from Omens of the Deep, if you own that expansion)

Components from base game+Unseen Forces
----------------------------------------
All Adventure cards from base+Unseen Forces
combined Mythos deck from base game+Unseen Forces
The Lost&Found Entrance card

*The other Entrance cards from Unseen Forces are not used

Setup:

1)Remove the following 5 cards from the Mythos deck. 

Fresh Start...Or Needed Aid
Hopeless...Or Doomed
Lost...Or Found
Unarmed...Or Unsafe
The Way Closes...Or Darkness Descends
------------------------------------------------------------------------ 
2)Adventure cards are placed faceup as per the usual rules.


3)Other World Cards enter play facedown, and whenever an Other World card is drawn, a gate appears, as per the rules in Gates of Arkham.

*An Other World card will only be placed faceup if it entered play as a result of a beneficial card (such as Gate Box or Find Gate). 


4)Put the Streets of Arkham Entrance sheet in play, and place your investigators on it. 


5)In the beginning of the game, place an Event card facedown at random on two of the six starting adventures.

6) Whenever a doom token is added to the regular non-gate/non-monster space on the doom track, place a facedown Event card on any Museum adventure at random that doesn't already have one.

7)
There can never be more than 3 Event cards in play on Museum Adventures 

8) If you've failed or didn't complete a Museum Adventure with an Event card on it(after revealing the Event card), replace the Event card with a different one, until the Adventure has been resolved and/or replaced. 

9)
If you've used the Entrance sheet's ability to replace a Museum Adventure with A Midnight effect , add a doom token to the doom track.

10)When using common or unique items that add dice,you must commit to adding the yellow or red die to your dice pool before starting your resolution phase. 
[/b]

11)
Once per turn, whenever you use the yellow or red die for the completion of a task, if you roll the "4 investigation" or "wildcard" results, respectively, you may immediately take a free trip to the Lost&Found without risk of losing stamina/sanity.
The roll must be natural , and cannot be augmented or manipulated by any items or special abilities
Roll 3 green dice to see what you get. If you roll investigation results, you lose nothing. 

After resolving this, carry on with the completion of your task, as if your turn hasn't been interrupted. 
You may not use the Lost &Found in any other way, other than the one outlined above.

12)
Membership cards are not used, and any cards that denote them are discarded without effect. 
------------------------------------------------------------------------
We've been playing with this variant a lot to get extra mileage out of the base set, and it's very fun."

RATING: 6.5
Elder Sign is a lot of fun - it's basically a fairly simple push-your-luck dice game that plays great solo.  It has the flavor of Arkham Horror with a much shorter playing time.  As much as I enjoyed the game, though, its downfall was simplicity.  While Arkham Horror can be very tough with 1 or 2, Elder Sign is too easy!  Even as a solo game, I managed to win 80% of the time, and with 2 or more it seems like a no-brainer.  Sadly, until they manage to ramp up the difficulty on this one, it has hit the sale pile.

RATING: 3

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
I was positively surprised by this game. Having tried Eldritch Horror, Betrayal at House on the Hill and other games in that vein, I had low expectations coming into this game. However, it wasn’t as bad a game as I had thought. Sure, there is a LOT of dice rolling, and if you roll poorly you will lose the game no matter how well you play. Normally, I’m not a fan of this, but I think I didn’t mind too much because this is a cooperative game, so bad rolls affected the entire group instead of an individual. Also, the game is relatively short (we finished our games in about 50 and 40 minutes), and that’s a big plus for me. Eldritch Horror, based on the same theme, has a lower rating because it takes forever to play. 

Still, my rating of 5 reflects my opinion about the game; it’s an okay game, and I could play it once in a while, but I wouldn’t actively suggest it myself. If looking for a coop taking a little less than an hour, I would pick some other game (even if it ran a little longer). The gameplay simply feels too limited; you pick a monster to fight and hope you get those symbols when rolling and re-rolling. I did like how you could buy and get equipment once you’ve slain some monsters, but it felt a little weird that you could buy the necessary victory points. In my two games, we were never in any big trouble, so the ancient one never woke up (i.e. we won prematurely). I don’t like my coops too easy, so it will probably take a while before I play ES again.

RATING: 5
This game gets a 1 for playtesting because each of the games I've played have been a TOTAL cakewalk.  The reason I didn't give it 1 is because, underlying the game are fun mechanisms and items and such.  The problem is that there's almost no way for the doom track on the GOOs to fill up, certainly not with the mythos deck.  The mythos deck usually gives you an "out" for the doom token that is simple to take.  What an incredible shame.  This could have been awesome.

Update: I've begun playing with the following variants: each time you fail to complete a task, you take the penalty, even if dropping a die to re-roll; and share out monsters evenly (no piling on one poor card).  The game is now much harder, with much more interesting decisions.  Once I've tried it this way enough, I might change my rating.

RATING: 6
A bit put off by reports of typos, but a mythos game you can play in less than 5 hours?  Win!

Win?!  Yes, we certainly won.  Now that I've played I can add my voice to the other slightly-energetic meh's being uttered.  Although the game moves quickly enough and is usually fun, there's very limited strategy.  Do-nothing turns are frequent, and while they don't take too long it's sort of a bore to accomplish nothing in a turn.  Although bad stuff continued to happen, I never felt we were on the verge of defeat, although it was exciting when an excellent die roll brought us victory.

As an aside the lack of permanent equipment really detracts, for me, from the involvement I feel in building the character up.  Although the special abilities are nice, I had very little feeling of it being "my" character.

Overall I'd play it again, and enjoy it.  It doesn't suffer from the time issues that other mythos games do, but it doesn't really shine either.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Elder Sign on its own:
The base game is fun a but little easy for a solo/co-operative game.  It is still possible with the locked dice mechanism and a lot monsters appearing to go from a winning path to loosing.  However the tension generated in the Arkham Horror game can be absent as you pick your way through the locations faster than the doom track can escalate.  In fact I could not recommend playing this game without the expansion it may spoil your enjoyment.

The Expansion Unseen Forces:
This expansion makes all the difference it resets the difficulty just a little higher, even if you win its does not look like a fore gone conclusion. 

Variety and difficulty win win.

Elder Sign with the Expansion:
Arkham Yatzee is the most reductive way of looking at this game.  Although this is in part quite true, this game is not Roll Through the Ages which really does feel like a unashamed re-theme of Yatzee.

Tactically this game is a series of linked Yatzee like rounds used to resolve events.  This has its appeal but it is the decisions around when and how resources should be used (spells, items, character powers, clues etc) where to go next what should be made a priority (elder signs, blessings, midnight events, resource gathering etc) that makes this game only a distant relative of Yatzee.

The selection of a srategy is core and the most significant gameplay DNA it shares with Arkham Horror.  Without this the family resembalance would largely be artwork and theme.  Tactically a intuitive or mathimatical understanding of dice rolling probabilites will be required to make the best decissions. When you a rolling muliple dice at least a command of probability can be used to manage uncertainty.  I would go as far as saying that playing this game well requires the undestanding of probability in the way that Power Grid makes demands on your mental arithmatic (command of uncertainty can be demanding as certainty).

By the end of long game you will have estimated your chances picked 6 green dice and rolled a lot.  I think that Elder Sign can outstay its welcome and the simple core mechanic repeated endlessly can be an issue.

Arkham Horror Comparison:
My biggest criticisms of Arkham Horror is slow pace which means that a plan that takes minutes to devise can end up taking hours to implement and the slow death by a thousand cuts (the game can take a long time (sometimes hours) to go from a clear losing position to game completion.  

Arkham Horror still lingers in the memory like no other boardgame, a year later you can remember a close game, characters that played well and events that spun the game around.  Variety and randomness is everything, even the enjoyability of the game can be down to cards and dice.  If only the game could detect your loosing position and finish you off quickly.

Elder Signs suffers from the same issues but on a much smaller scale.  Plan to implementation, significantly quicker but still slow.  Losing or winning position to game end very variable and potentially slow.  Elder Sign suffers from the same weaknesses and its sister game but scaled down.

The player avatars feel less well defined and many of the items simply add one dice even if the artwork and name are different.  The Yatzee resolution and the less well defined characters and items can take you out of the game world and make it the game feel a little abstract at times.

Conclusion:
This is a worthwhile if not brilliant re-implementation of the Arkham Horror paradigm.  It shares many of Arkham Horrors faults on a smaller scale and the strengths  also feel sightly watered down.  Arkham Lite just seems to fit the bill.

FFG are having yet another go at an Arkham game.  I can only hope that it has the same strenghts as its predecessors scaled up and they manage to water down the weaknesses.  Until then I will keep on watching the sky.

Não consigo parar de jogar!
Um jogo cooperativo de rolagem de dados de mistério e suspense no universo de Lovecraft.
A mecânica é diferente dos outros jogos que temos, apesar dos componentes se assemelharem com de Eldritch Horror.
Aqui, temos locais revelados nas cartas, onde apresentam desafios para conseguir a recompensa. A cada turno, escolhemos qual local visitar com nosso personagem, que, se completar todos os desafios do local com os limitados dados disponíveis (e uma possível ajuda externa), consegue as recompensas da carta, que podem ser itens para o personagem, marcadores de progresso na missão ou mesmo surgimento de novos monstros ou avanço da perdição. O objetivo é aprisionar o Ancião antes de ele despertar, ou, se despertar, tentar sobreviver à impossível batalha final. A ambientação é incrível.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 1
Traded this, not sure you could call it a game. This is a very overrated game. Up to the standard of FFG, card typos, which take away from the game, rules unclear, example when do you play a spell, 6 months for a FAQ from FFG, has very little cooperative play. Basically you collect items, which you can't trade, these basically just allow you to freeze die, or small die change, you pick a adventure card and you roll until you win or lose, lose you take a hit, adventure card may get harder via of adding a monster. Cooperative play is if another investigator failed the card first, is still sitting on it, you can freeze a die on him, they called it focus. This is just Yahtzee with some cards for ever increase goals for the dice to meet. It is clear FFG didn't proofread the text on the cards before printing and given the rules, didn't bother to test play with a fresh group of players with the final draft of the rule book. Just read the rule forum posts before that 6 months FAQ came out. Only the Lovecraft, FFG and the Arkham Horror fanboys must keep this game's rating up. You can't get pass that you just reading off some probability off a card and rolling dices to win or lose, over and over, losing one or more die each roll, feels like playing craps with variable probability. The choices seem pretty transparent. Why is this fun? It feels more like a chore playing. As for cards adding theme, why, or why, do they print in fonts that are hard to read? It adds nothing to the games as the theme is oil on water. At the price of Forbidden Island this game might be worth picking up, I wouldn't. At the $30 I paid this wasn't worth it, the card typos which changed play, the poor rule book, with the FAQ, corrected info for the cards, it is playable, still not fun, and these things just adds insult to injury. I will think long and hard before buying another FFG game when it first comes out, or at all. The other game publishers just seem to put more of an effort into their products, they are quicker on a FAQ, I have seen some publishers answer questions, not so FFG, they just let you house rule it, until they get to a FAQ. It looks like FGG just phoned in Elder Sign. If you purchased this early, without the idevice app, anyone remember the question of when a spell could be used, game vs app, and 6 month in the making FAQ helping you out, this game wasn't a gaming experience as much as it was an experiment. Using early buyers to sort out your rule book isn't my idea of a good business model. This is what fresh test players are for. 

The only horror in this game is the production, rule book, game play, created it would seem via of  FGG's we phoned it in test play, which produced game playing card typos and a rule book that is only of value if you know the rules. That or they just don't care. If you turned this in as a high school project I would question if it would even get a D just based on the production. Will be glad when this one fades away.

Interesting reading comments at the 7 rating. Why do people have short reviews, like "boring watching other people roll", "lots of down time", "dice fest", "yahtzee", "after 3 or 4 games, not hitting the table, boring" and rate it a 7? Do they know what a 7 means?

Learning to take ratings numbers with a grain of salt. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.75
What's not to love? This is a slimmed down version of one of my favorite games (Arkham Horror) but it plays in less than half the time. There are a lot less stats to keep track of, and visually the challenges are clear even to the novice player.

I also appreciate that you keep the classic characters, each bringing a special ability which is often critical to your success. With the different big villains to fight, you have the opportunity to scale it up to the difficulty level your group prefers.  And you can play this solo.

Honestly the only real drawbacks are that the luck element is very high because it's all dice-based, and there are a relatively limited number of challenge cards.  Fortunately this is ripe for expansions.  While I still love AH, I expect will play Elder Sign far more often.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
DIGITAL PLAY:

iPad Air
1 Player Minimum
8 Player Maximum
Digital and Physical Game

Set Up Notes for Base Game with Unseen Forces expansion:
1.) Set Clock to Midnight.
2.) Place Entrance Sheets:
-First Aid Station
-The Chapel
-Lost and Found
-Souvenir Shop
3.) Prepare Dice, Tokens, Cursed/Blessed cards and Monsters.
4.) Randomly choose one Ancient One.
5.) Shuffle Adventure Deck and deal SIX Adventure Cards face up.
6.) Shuffle:
    -Common Items
    -Unique Items
    -Spells
    -Allies
    -Other World Deck
    -Mythos Deck
5.) Select and Set up Investigator Cards with starting Items and corresponding Tokens.
6.) Resolve initial Mythos Card. 
7.) Begin Game!

Rules Notes:
-INITIAL MYTHOS CARD is resolved before game begins.
-REVEALING ADVENTURE CARDS: Watch for Locked Dice icons and Special Text.
-ORDER ARROW: Arrow point Down on Adventure Cards means tasks must be completed in order.
-PLACING MONSTER: must be placed on white spaces first, bottom of cards equally if no white spaces are available.
-DEFEAT MONSTER: Monster Trophies are gathered at the end of Resolution Phase, BEFORE penalty or reward from Adventure Card occurs.
-TASK COMPLETION: May complete only ONE Task per roll.
-CURSED DICE removes one green dice with correspond icon from Dice Pool.
-ADVENTURE CARD SUCCESS: Draw new Adventure Card BEFORE collecting reward.
-WIZARD WHATELEY: Adds an Order Arrow to the Adventure Card placed at.
-RESTRICTED: Yello exclamation means to not use unless playing with specific expansion.
-FOCUS: Only Focus if it is a failed roll. One dice must be removed for failed before a Focus.


I enjoy both games because they differ enough to have both in my collection. The digital does not have allies and you can only play 4 investigators instead of 8. The digital has some really neat scenario driven adventures that offer new game play mechanics. The digital does not have an end game battle with the ancient one if you don't collect enough elder signs.

RATING: 7
 Cthulhu dice saves the world! Or not?

 Arkham Horr... ehm, cooperative Arkham Yathzee, but not quite. Theme is strong, atmosphere also and it´s such a fun to roll dice in attempt to save the world. Big win of this game is, that (luckily) you are not dependent just on pure luck, because you have possibilies (through cards with represent allies, magic or equipment) how to work with each (ehm, most) dice rolls. It´s much more fun than it seems on the start. And despite light horror theme, it´s perfectly suitable as a great family game (with older children), which is not a euro trash nor a american trash.

 Component value is high, but not top notch (I can imagine better dice; they are quality enough, but feels light to me and not much suitable to theme). Rules are simple, but there is classic FFG "grey zone" in them, when particualy situations can be interpreted in more ways and rules doesn´t give you a straight answer "how you suppose to play it".

 Only one bigger flaw is difficulty, which is too low on cooperative game and even too low for casual gamers. On the other side, system is so well conceived an open to tinker, that you have tons of possibilites to make your own house rules (or there are lots of very good variants) without changing a game core mechanism (much). Fhtagn!

RATING: 8
Some people call this game Cthulhu Yahtzee, but I think it plays more like a light dungeon crawler. You've got health and sanity points, you've got spells and items to tip the scales in your favor, and you've got lots of dice to do battle with unspeakable horrors! With a thick Lovecraft theme and about a 90 minute playing time, what's not to love? It's a good price with quality bits, too.

This game is a huge hit with my kids and myself. We play it almost any chance we've got the time available.

RATING: 7.9
Thematically very nicely crafted cooperative game, in which the players are investigators in the monster infested city of Arkham. A lot of different characters can be played, each with their own sanity and stamina level, and specific abilities. There are lots of different cards representing weapons, artifacts, spells, allies... Random events are taking place when entering specific locations, each 12 hours is played under specific circumstances, and on top of that a host of adventure cards are available all adding to the replayability of this dice driven game. If you don't like to be at the mercy of the dice gods, play another game, otherwise a great deal of tension and fun is guaranteed.

I love that this game can play up to 8, as there aren't a lot of games  that can handle that many players. It still works equally well with less.  Now don't  mistake that to mean this game is easy to win. Oh no, far from it, but that's part of what I like about it. It requires a combination of luck,  cooperation and managing of tools to emerge victorious, but even when you lose, it's usually still a fun game. Besides, it isn't Lovecraft if the horrors don't usually win, right? 

There is one scary thing that happens though. When playing at the local game store, I usually have an employee blind pick the elder god we face. Every time the store manger has picked, we've faced Shub-Niggurath after he called it as he picked it each time.

RATING: 5
Fun dice probability game.  Some people say there is too much luck, but there are enough choices in when and how to roll the dice that this is very overstated.

In fact, number of choices is a strength of the game as you must constantly analyze your odds and choose the dice strategy that gives the best chance of success at the end of the series of rolls.

That said, it has the usual coop game caveats: luck in terms of card/monster draw can make the game too easy or too hard and the actions you take to win tend toward the repetitive.

RATING: 8
My first and most important thought was this is what LOTR LCG should be like. this game is so much fun. I can aquire gear, recruit allies, get spells,heal up, turn in points to get even more gear,  and not to mention each hero's ability is great.

There are no bad decisions to make only which of many usefull/good decisions to make to get the job done. now some would say this is too easy, but I would take none of that. I think (just my opinion) that this could be considerd easy as in 'I win every time'. However, I think the more correct way of looking at it is 'how can I get this won without taking longer to do it? 

maybe I can put that another way....this isn't pass/fail (where people want it a 20/80 to be considered difficult and challenging ala Dugeonquest). I think ES more a game of a grade: You either get it done quickly (given an A) or less so (B,C,D where the 'punishment' is a longer game to get it done) with the unlikly event of dying if your totaly unlucky and get that ill fated F grade.

The co-op is seemless, helpful, and fun to work together, the events are managable and not increasingly devasting with each passing turn (and no threat wheel).  I really enjoyed the game, and I know I loved it because all I wanted to do afterwards was play again.

I have never played Arkahm Horror, but after playing this I sure want to now.

Elder Sign is a cooperative game where the players work together to kill monsters.  On your turn, you can pick what you want to attack and can tailor your decision based upon your role (and special power that comes with it) and your special cards.  This game is challenging to win, but is doable.  You have one last chance to kill the main monster, but if you get to that point you are unlikely to win.  Players like the ability to chose what part of the mission they are going to go after.

RATING: 9
Egyenlőre egyedül próbáltam ki a játékot 4 karaktert (nyomozót) indítva, hogy tisztába legyek a szabályokkal, mire másoknak is bemutatom. Elöljáróban annyit mondanék, hogy nagyon tetszik a játék, pedig nem ismerem Lovecraft világát és nem is annyira jön át a téma, viszont a kellő feszültséget teremtő játékmenet és a folyamatos sikerélmény (a kalandlapok megoldása által), kiemeli a kockás játékok átlagából (már amennyit én ismerek). A játék szabálya nem túl egyszerű, mégis pár játék után tökéletesen elsajátítható, habár ezzel ellentmond, hogy én a harmadik játékom alkalmával is valamit hibásan játszottam (igaz, ezzel inkább magamnak nehezítettem meg a játékot). Azt mondják, hogy a játék túl könnyű, én nem ezt vettem észre. Az egyik játékban egyszerre szereztem meg az utolsó ősi jelet és végzet sáv jelzőt, amivel éppen csak nyertem. Egy másikban pedig maratoni küzdelemben győztem le a Mérhetetlen Vént, ahol ugyan nem forgott veszélyben a felébredése, mégis két nyomozóm is halálát lelte a Miskatonic egyetem múzeumában. A játékra az van írva, hogy a játékidő 90 perc. Bizonyosan ennyi idő alatt is le lehet játszani, azonban én sokat görcsöltem (időt töltöttem el) azon, hogy akkor most melyik nyomozómat melyik kalandra küldjem, kihasználva a képességeiket és a megszerzett javakat. Így nekem nem sikerült levinnem 3 óra alá a játékidőt, habár még sokszor olvasgattam a játékszabályt ás a hivatalos FAQ-ot tisztázás végett (mondom, így is elhibáztam egy-kettőt). Végeredményben aki elfogadja a kockákból eredő szerencse faktort és egy kicsi szerepjátékos beütéssel bír, vagy csak szeret kalandozni képzelt világokban, valamint szereti a folyamatos feszültséget a kockadobások pozitív kimenetelét remélve és képes csapatjátékban gondolkozni, annak nagyon jó szívvel ajánlom ezt a gyönyörű grafikával ékesített, jó minőségű, kiváló játékot. Vesszen Cthulhu! :) (2014.10.23)

RATING: 9
Having never played Arkham Horror or Mansions of Madness, I will review this game based solely on its own merit, not a comparison as most people have done. That being said, I have seen AH and MoM played at conventions, and they seem really complex with lots of things to keep track of. This game, however, is pretty simple, perhaps too simple for some. This really is just Yatzee Chthulhu, thats a pretty good name for it. Luckily, I love Yatzee and I love H.P. Lovecraft, so this was an instant success in my house. What I really like about this game is that adults and kids can play it together and can both have fun for different reasons. The adults can pretend to be hunting monsters, while the kids can enjoy finally being able to play one of "Daddy's Games" without having to have their hand held the entire time.

Another thing I like about, is the rules can be tweeked. Having too much trouble, hand out some extra clues or spell cards. Too easy, add some extra doom tokens. There really is no reason to bash this game on the rules when you can easily change them and make the game better. My only gripe is the lack of diversity of your items. You get Spells, Unique Items, Common Items, and Allies, but they all basically allow you to do the same things. So, my question is, why bother with all the different kind of cards, why not just have an items pile, with all those mixed in, like Last Night on Earth?

Bottom line, enjoyable, but slightly flawed.

RATING: 5
Elder Sign was Yahtzee Arkham Horror where you do generally similar things but the game loses all of it's theme and narrative arc to save time. It also commits one of the what I consider to be Cardinal Sins of game design: when a card/tile has a different name/picture than another card but is 100% identical mechanically. What is the point in this? Visual variety? Ugh! This game suffers in that regard in a major way when you look at the various cards investigators can collect. Anyway, as long as it was a 2 - 4 player I would almost always choose Arkham Horror over this... especially playing events in a 'Tales of Arabian Nights' sort of story telling. If it was more players, I'd probably rather suffer through Elder Signs.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
A simple game but maybe too simple. It seems to devolve to just rolling good dice and hoping for the best, as there aren't enough levers for players to operate. You get to add at most two dice at any one time, few cards can change the dice roll, and where you can go is determined randomly.

And for a co-op, there aren't enough hard choices to make. Part of the thrill of great co-ops like Lord of the Rings is the dilemma of weighing the risks or the impact of bad consequences and trying to decide which is the best option. But you don't get it here. The tension relies purely on whether you get the dice rolls or not and there's nothing special about that. I can get that with any dice-rolling game.

While Witch of Salem has its flaws, the game still gives you a sense that strategy matters. Not so here.

P.S. On the rulebook issue, I was taught the game but did have a chance to flip through the rulebook. It does seem unnecessarily obtuse, what with silly terminology like "focus". And as it seems that the go-to method of learning the game is to watch video reviews, and not actually read the rulebook, that says a lot about the state of the rulebook.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Elder Sign is an awesome, albeit rather brutal dice rolling game.

The theming is beautiful, every component, the artwork, the flavour texts, gorgeous, even though the game feels fairly abstracted from the mechanics of the game.

The theme suffers somewhat mechanically for what is tantamount to Yahtzee, on crack, playing against the Devil; that didn't stop FFG from putting every effort and resource into making the theme as strong as possible.

The game is ultimately down to luck; the push your luck element is definitely there but you aren't trapped by it.  Players can choose their battles, collect items, and work with their character's skill to skew odds in their favour.  

If you aren't a gambler have ever wondered how gambling addicts get into deep water, play this game, "Just one more roll, I know I can do this!...  Ok, this time!"

Elder Sign is fantastic value for money and plays as well solo as it does in groups.

I think this is truly the beauty of this game, you take on a role as a heroic investigator with some ability but most of the time you are just an useless human against all the odds, so the best way to survive in the apocalypse is man up and give all you got and go all or nothing on a mission you were sign up for. It's lots of luck but it can be blended in the theme

RATING: 3
This really feels like a phoned-in design that's taking advantage of a popular license.  Yes the production is top notch but the game play lacks any real tension or decision making.  

Yahtzee is a better game than this.  In Elder Sign players roll a hand of six dice against their choice of adventure. This is really where the decisions stop.  Players then look at the dice to see whether or not they have completed any of the assigned tasks on the card.  If the symbols match you rolled well.  Then you take the remaining dice and roll again to see if you accomplished any of the remaining tasks.  Rinse and repeat for rounds after rounds.  

Elder scroll offers no push-your-luck or any real decision making.  You can't decide to hold off and score your progress.  Nor does it ever really make any sense not to complete a task if you have rolled the right symbols.  Yeah okay, once in a while you lose a sanity or stamina point, or a monster appears (these are dealt with in the same way as any other task) but the game play is nothing more than rolling dice and checking the result.  All the additions just disguise the poor design here.

NO REAL CHOICES.

THIS IS BARELY A GAME.  

A major disappointment for me after Richard Launius' masterful Defenders of the Realm.  

Initial feeling was this game had maybe three or four plays in it and rated a 5.  With thought I have no desire to play again after checking the rules to confirm we played correctly.  

I rate this a lowly 3

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Love the fact that this can be played solo.  Fantastic components, very dynamic gameplay.  Really communicates the feeling of Arkham Horror but with a much shorter set up and game play.

Contrary to what others have said, I don't think that it feels like Yahtzee (although I happen to like Yahtzee).  The dice rolls streamline the process of AH, but they still feel like you're trying to accomplish the tasks at hand.  

One challenge of the game is that there are so many little nuances and details that it's easy to forget one--advance the clock, mythos card at midnight, terror effect, dice locks, etc.  Still, getting used to the system alleviates a lot of it.

Haven't tried this with Unseen Forces yet.  I've heard it really adds to the game, but I'm trying to get a good grasp of the base game before adding expansion.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I've been dodging Arkham Horror for a while now. I've loved HP Lovecraft's fiction for quite some time but the length of the board game would NOT go over well with my friends and it's much too long for me to play solo. 
Along comes this game. It was a bit of an impulse buy to push my order up for free shipping but I'm really glad I picked this up. 
The rulebook is one of FFG's easier books to make sense of, the gameplay is simple and I have waaay more choices available to me than Death Angel! This definitely captures the feel of a larger co-op (Defenders of the Realm/Ghost Stories) but seems much quicker to set up and finish tasks. Solo, this game may present the D&D boardgames and Runebound with some serious competition.
Addressing the "too easy" comments: this game is soooo modular, there are many tweaks you could do to add to the difficulty. Eliminate the clue tokens as a re-roll option, move the clock (turns) in larger increments (4-6 hours instead of 3)...
This game is also quite expandable. More adventure cards, more investigators, monsters...I could even imagine adding quest-like (goals?) adventure cards mixed in at fixed points in the adventure deck. Maybe I should work for FFG...;)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

I started playing Elder Sign on the Android app and was hooked instantly.  It's an intense game that's mostly luck-based but involves some simple strategy as well.  It's like Lovecraftian gambling in a way.  

I bought the base set hoping to lure my gaming groups into playing and while I got a couple of plays out of it (and thoroughly enjoyed it) it doesn't come out too often.  The group tends to want to get into the more involved gameplay of Arkham Horror or Mansions of Madness.  

Setup takes a bit of time, so even though solo play is an option I'll just turn to the app instead.

RATING: 3
This is everything that Arkham Horror should have been;
cleaner playing, less fiddly, faster turns, yet wholly thematic.
The wife and I both enjoyed this much more than AH. I didn't forget anything, which I often do whilst playing AH; flip Mythos cards, resolve certain world effects, move the terror, add doom tokens, etc.

I found the pared down rules and simplicity much more engaging than AH, and there was much less to remember, calculate and fiddle with.

Overall, a very good dice game.

After a few years, and a bunch of plays, I can't seem to bring myself to like this game.
I think it's TOO random, even though I like randomness in my games. This game though, heaps random cards, on top of random items, allies, and gear, and then you randomly determine if you can complete randomly drawn adventures/quests.

There is so much random here that all expansions can do is ratchet up the difficulty each time a new one comes out. Or make it stand-alone at this point.

It's a mediocre random-fest that's not worth the effort. I've had games end after two turns due to random stacking of effects, and just the opposite - winning the game in 4 turns, which ruins the entire experience.

I'm putting this up for trade in case there's anyone out there that wants this, as I can no longer derive enjoyment from playing this.

RATING: 3
This game tries to combine the Cthulhu Mythos atmosphere with light gaming mechanics - and fails miserably.  There is no atmosphere here, just plain and stupid dice rolling.  

At the end of the day, each and every "adventure" task of the investigators can be reduced to:  take x dice and roll y fixed combinations in z attempts.  That's it.  Meaningful decisions?  More or less non existent.  And to make a mediocre game even worse, there is way too much luck.  Good rolls accelerate the game, giving you addional re-rolls, additional dice etc.  Bad rolls deny you any resources, making the game slower and slower and more painful from round to round.  

Being a fan of games like Vegas, Kingsburg or Alien Frontiers, I have no problem with dice whatsoever but this game really drags if you have bad luck and that is a pain in the ***.

Furthermore they call it a cooperative game.  Where's the cooperation?  You can't trade resources, you can't gang up on monsters and you can pursue different ways to victory.

Bottom line: from all Cthulhu based games I've played, this is by far the worst.  Never again!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Arkham Horror's flaws are well documented at this point.  While still loved by many, Fantasy Flight has been working on a series of games that deliver the best elements of Arkham Horror without the long play, the complicated set-up, and the impenetrable rule book.

So far, this is my favorite.

Like its predecessor, Elder Sign pits a team of investigators against the supernatural horrors of the universe.  They must succeed at challenges in order to collect Elder Signs that they will use to prevent a powerful Ancient One from devouring our world.  This is done with the help of clues and magical items.

Admittedly, this games does not offer nearly the same scope as Arkham Horror.  While Arkham Horror spanned an entire city and had a great variety of items and encounters, Elder Sign is confined to a museum.  Encounters and items may have different names, but this is mostly for flavor.  Many of them are virtually identical.  The encounters themselves are all mechanically very similar.  The flavor seems to come mostly from the artwork and the text, which will come as a disappointment to fans of the original game.

However, Elder Sign sacrifices theme for streamlined play.  The core challenge system is very easy to understand.  Someone watching a group play could probably understand at least the basic concept.  Role custom dice and try to match the symbols on the dice to the symbols on the challenge.  If you fail, throw away one dice and try again.  Lose all your dice, and suffer the consequences!

While it may not be as flavorful as Arkham Horror's RPG-ish stat system, it's simplicity really plays into it's strength as a cooperative game.  Any player can watch you role for a challenge and understand how well you are doing without necessarily knowing your characters abilities.  This makes it very easy for your teammates to feel emotionally invested in the success of your challenge.  In every game I have played, players have been huddled around the board watching the dice with great interest, cheering good roles and groaning at bad roles.  This is exactly the kind of comradery you want a cooperative game to generate, and it puts the game in stark contrast with Arkham Horror, a game in which a feels like each player plays in isolation.  There may be a few moments of shared enthusiasm, but the game can't sustain it indefinitely.

Granted, Elder Sign couldn't be exciting for 6-8 hours either, but it has the good sense to end in quarter of that amount of time.

Elder Sign may not pack all of the theme of Arkham Horror, but it delivers many of the games best elements in a smaller more manageable package that, and this is the bottom line, you will actually be able to bring to the table.  If you are looking for a Lovecraft-themed cooperative game, I strongly recommend this one.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
This was one of my must-buys of Gencon 2011, and even though I paid a bit more than the online pre-order folks, I have no regrets.

Very good push-your-luck dice game in the vein of Arkham Horror.  The theme is appropriately smaller from the main game of Arkham Horror, taking place in a museum rather than in an entire town.  The tasks and pressure, however, are no less dire. 

In our first game, we won handily, though frequent checks back to the rulebook made me wonder if we missed out on a rule or two.  Regardless, the game is fun, with plenty of interesting and difficult decisions to make along the way. 

The rule book can be confusing at points, and I'm sure that a FAQ would clear it up nicely.

Right now I think I would still prefer to play the original if conditions (namely time) allowed, but this is a great lighter, quicker alternative that scratches much of the same itch.

RATING: 7.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Perhaps the best dice-game I have. I call it a dice-game, because the great majority of things in this game are done via dice. Whether it's actions or fighting, it's rolling dice. Some could find this alienating, too much luck-dependent, and they aren't too wrong I guess. But, in a game like this, it's more like risk-evaluation, you have to calculate when it's worth the risk to do something and when it is not. And usually you have at least some tools to modify your die results or even re-roll your dice. 
Anyway, that about the mechanics. The game is Lovecraftian co-op game, strong theme of horror, mystery, occult and impending doom here. You take the role of various people, with different professions, backgrounds and abilities etc. You then start exploring Arkham Museum during night time, in order to stop a cosmic-terror to awake and stop the end of the world. Small things, eh? No pressure. So you look for clues, items and other stuff that could help you, at the same time occasionally fighting with cultists and other ugly bastards from some dusty corridors of the museum. The whole bunch of gameplay comes from moving from the room to the other room and doing all the things that are required to be done in the said room, in order to advance. Sometimes you can go back to the exit and heal yourself etc. 
This is one of those co-op's that are really tense and keep you on your toes all the time. You really have to think about your actions, because time is a great enemy. There's only a certain amount of time before the Ancient One awakens, so there's no time to loiter around. Even one mistake in this game can easily lead to at least that characters demise, but also make you loose the entire game. This game is also very challenging. The only bad thing is that sometimes you have that feeling that bad roll results of the dice are ruining your game more than failed actions etc. That's just something that has to be tolerated when playing dice-games. Still, perhaps that mechanic could have been a bit less relentless. 
As usual the game looks stunningly good, for FFG game. Cards are detailed in their art work, dice are good quality etc. Only component related complain must be given from not including proper figures. Now there's only very small and flat cardboard tokens representing your characters. Would it really have been so difficult to have figures? I don't think so.
Even so a brilliant co-op game for everyone who love the theme and doesn't mind some random elements in his survivor-horror-world-saving co-op game.

RATING: 7
I love the thematics of this game. The art, well I've seen it a billion times in between Call of Cthulhu the card game and the Arkham Horror set, but it still looks badass.

The dice part of the game is fun. Yes, there's luck in this game, but the game is about mitigating your bad luck as much as possible. For the amount of time you have to explain the game, and the depth you get out of that, it's pretty good.

I wish the items did different stuff. I wish there was an expansion to improve parts of the game which I felt were underwhelming.

There is little reason to pay attention to other people's turns, unless you want to watch and be amused. There is no interaction between players needed, but players seem to do so anyways.

For what the game sets out to do, it succeeds.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
[b]Rating & comments are for the 1st Printing with the screwed up rulebook; the Revised (2012) Printing gets a 7.[/b]

[b]tl;dr[/b] — As an [gameid=15987] & dice game fan I like what it does, though rules & timing ambiguities keep it from being great.  Like [i]AH[/i] expect to play it entirely wrong the first couple times, and then find it far too easy once you do get the rules down.

[b]tl;dr After the FAQ:[/b]  A kinder, gentler [i]Arkham[/i]—and not in the good way—this game is mild and crazy-easy.  The first printing is a total loss.

[b]Progression through the first 10 plays with the rules out of the box (pre-FAQ first printing):[/b]

[b]Thoughts after one play:[/b]  I'm pretty sure that all the various reports of "too easy/too hard" are due to incorrect play (a critical issue with other co-ops like [gameid=823], [gameid=37046] & [gameid=30549])—missing a single, small rule* or even just altering the order of certain events** could make the entire system cascade in one direction or the other.

The rulebook is needlessly obtuse for what is essentially a push-your-luck dice game—[i]assemble dice pool, roll, bank or re-roll[/i] shouldn't be so hard to explain.  We hit many, many rules ambiguities in our first play, several of which were only answered with a very careful line-by-line rereading of the rules afterward, as the answers were often a single sentence hidden inside a paragraph, and thus easily missed.  Still other questions await an offical FAQ.

Other than that the game is pretty, the components excellent, and rolling dice is fun.  Also, I think no fewer than three people got eaten by the Shoggoth in the Koi Pond.

[i]Nice.[/i]

[b]After 3 plays:[/b]  The key to all push-your-luck dice games is, of course, banking and re-rolls.  It took a couple plays to figure out when and where this is possible, as the rulebook is less than effective at spelling (hah) it out.

[b]• Success = keep going[/b]
You can keep rolling as long as you are successfully completing tasks, but, of course, that shrinks the pool, making future tasks more difficult.

[b]• Clues[/b]
Clues are HUGE as they are the primary mechanism that lets you bank and re-roll.  Spend a clue to re-roll any or all of the dice in the pool.  Most games of this ilk allow a certain number of bank/re-rolls—e.g., three in [i]Yahtzee[/i]—but here you're limited to how many clues you have.

[b]• Focus/Assist[/b]
You can bank a single die on yourself, or a single die on a fellow Investigator on the same Adventure card... but you must fail to complete a task first.  A small booby prize, though with the die you lose for failure you're down two dice in the pool, so it's a gamble.

[b]• Spells[/b]
Cast before the roll (a dangerous gamble) and bank one or two dice out of a roll (though this could be brutally bad if you are [i]required[/i] to bank).  Post-FAQ update:  Spells are now cast [i]after[/i] the roll, to bank dice you already know you want to keep.  Does the double-whammy of making the game easier (?!) and removing any downside to spells—removing all thematic coherence.  Lovecraftian spells are supposed to be dangerous, but it's all happy fairy magic now.

[i]Elder Sign[/i] doesn't feel like a true push-your-luck experience until you understand how to pull off clever combos with all these mechanisms.  Then the game really opens up and delivers.

Still, as a tuned co-op machine it misfires badly if you forget the small rules*** or get the sequencing of certain choices or events wrong.  Looking very forward to an offical FAQ to clean this thing up.

[b]After [-]6[/-] [-]7[/-] 8 plays:[/b]  I [i]almost[/i] get the sense I'm playing it correctly.  Almost.

[b]After 9 plays:[/b]  Okay, I finally get it.  Elder Sign is a light, storytelling larf, along the lines of [gameid=27627], rather than a tight, cruel co-op engine like [gameid=30549].  Expectations reset accordingly. 

[b]Final Analysis:[/b]  Man, I wanted to love this game.  It's totally in my wheelhouse—Lovecraft, dice, quick co-op.  [b]But the first printing is a total loss.[/b]  The rulebook is wrong on several fundamental issues (spells, focus/assist, etc.), three of the characters need to have new rules scrawled on their cards, and the FAQ changes make the game stupid easy.

Lovecraft + co-op + easy = WTF?!

A good co-op needs to have an out-of-the box win-rate below 50% in order to bear repeat play—the tension of not knowing whether or not you're going to survive [i]is[/i] the game.  It also incentivizes "beating" the game and gives big emotional payback for a hard-fought win.  Elder Sign has none of this.  I'm not even sure we've ever lost.

Yes, I could make up rules to increase the difficulty but that's not what I paid FFG for.  If I wanted to make my own games, or houserule the hell out of the ones I own (and then blunder through personal playtesting to see if they work) then I'd be doing that.  If a game is a "make-your-own" kit then say so on the box.

[b]I'm sorry I was an early adopter on this one.[/b]  Rating dropped to a barely deserved 5.

[size=7]*Like adding a Doom Token to the Doom Track whenever an Investigator is devoured.

**Like what happens when you complete an Adventure card:

1.  Receive reward(s)
2.  Move Investigators to Entrance
3.  Remove dice & take card as trophy
4.  Draw new Adventure card

is important as monsters in the "reward" line cannot be put on the new Adventure card.  An easily missed, teeny-tiny detail.  Post-FAQ update:  Nope!  Monsters are now an exception and can be added to the new card.  This change does the double-whammy of making the game easier while adding an exception to the rules.  Just what it needed...

***"Lose sanity/stamina" is entirely different from "adjust your sanity/stamina"—thus, the stamina cost on something like the Hallway on Fire cannot be prevented with Food, for instance.  Another tiny detail that is merely implied by word-choice in the rules... and, upon closer inspection, the rules use both interchangeably.  So, the question is, can you use a steak dinner to save yourself from a fire?  Or kill a Ghost with Whiskey?  Post-FAQ update:  Yes.  Yes you can.[/size]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Replaying, rethinking, rerating the Revised (2012) Printing:

[b][thread=914653][/thread][/b]

[i]Elder Sign[/i] is really all about the pulpy, three-fisted flavor and the delicious tension that comes from a 5-in-6 chance of [i]instant doom[/i] as the lone bone rattles around in a sweaty fist and a depth of eyeballs stare...

...and for those rare moments of real catharsis when that 1-in-6 bit hits and the whole table erupts in exaltation.

[size=12][b]Investigators - 5, Mythos - 3[/b][/size]

[c]Solo - 3 (1-2)
 2p  - 1 (1-0)
 3p  - 1 (1-0)
 4p  - 1 (1-0)
 5p  - 1 (0-1)*
 6p  - 1 (1-0)[/c]

[b]62% Win Rate[/b]**

Includes:  [thing=137479]Unseen Forces[/thing], museum-appropriate bits from [thing=189807]Omens of Ice[/thing]

[size=7]*This play had an inordinate number of new players—three, I think—and we don't allow alpha-dogging in our co-ops.  A crack team of veterans would have won this one.

**Though without the solo games this jumps to 80%.  I consider solo play to be a degenerate variant as I play with a single character alone; Mr. Launius has stated elsewhere that the game is really "balanced" (or at least designed) for four characters at a time, recommending the full compliment for solo play.  I dislike the fiddly overhead of running an entire team by myself, and besides, the game is much more challenging with a single character.  And that's a good thing.[/size]

RATING: 7.5
Cthulhu yatzee! And that is not an insult.  So much fun.....
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
I enjoy King of Tokyo, Pandemic: The Cure and Bang! The Dice Game and I thought I would love Elder Sign, boy was I wrong. First off, dice games are fun, but they can feel boring after more than 35 minutes. Roll for the Galaxy is the exception since it's not a "dice chucker", but a literal Dice version of Race for the Galaxy that works incredibly well. Even still that game can be knocked out in 45 minutes.

In Elder Sign you have to get certain faces on your dice "yahtzee-style" to accomplish "goals/missions" on different cards. Sounds simple, reminds me of another game, Age of War. If you succeed then hooray you get rewards, such as clues, weapons, magic or an Elder Sign needed to seal away the ancient old one. But if you fail,  prepare thine anus. These effects are punishing and could result in an easy elimination, making this co-op game that much harder. Add-in the randomness of dice, having to get certain combinations to finish the 2-4 objectives in one go, having dice/items locked, having to complete objectives in a certain order, not to mention random monster spawns that make cards/mission harder and waking up the ancient one which make things, you guessed it, harder or just simply game over, and you got a game full of randomness, luck and punishing difficulty.

I know there are ways to mitigate dice, and lock in results to use in future turns. However locking a die result meant you rolled that much less in a turn or having to visit the in-game store to trade for them...and that's of course if you got them since it's randomly assorted and also wasted your turn since the clock runs three hours between turns. When the clock strikes midnight well guess what? Bad Stuff happens. Plus items are beyond basic. Roll a yellow die. Roll a red die. I mean they have common items and spells, but they're pretty much identical. 

There is a bit of nice variation with cards that can heal you or instantly kill an enemy but that makes up 4% of the cards. How about cards that allow you to not receive any negative effects this turn or prevent the Ancient One's special ability for one night or when midnight strikes? And Don't even get me started on cheap game ending mechanics, such as every time you roll a terror die, EVERYBODY loses 1 health. Wow I lost a game I had in the bag, because I rolled a terror die 4 times in a row. Stupid, Stupid Stupid random garbage right there.

The games plays 1-8 players....WHAT!!! Nothing changes either(surprise, surprise all these cthulhu crap games play ridiculous numbers). only play this with 1-3, maybe 4. The only thing that's added is about 20 minutes more per player. I can't even fathom anyone who would play this for more than 45 minutes before wanting to sacrifice themselves to the ancient ones themselves.

Sigh...I really wanted to like this game, but for what it is, I'll stick with King of Tokyo/New York and Bang! These are well played and liked in my group. Elder Sign fell flat instantly with everyone I introduced it to. Sold it and don't miss it at all. Picked up the app for 99 cents on my phone, and that is slightly better, cause I can finish it in about 15 minutes, but it can still be punishing, but for less than a buck i'm not going to complain.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A basic and moderately enjoyable, if rather too easily beaten, co-operative dice game. 

There's a distinct paucity in terms of the cards provided in the base game - all the better to encourage you to pick up the inevitable expansions one presumes - but what components are included are of the usual FFG quality (albeit with a great deal of recycled artwork). 

The problem here is that the game sells itself as being "inspired by the works of HP Lovecraft" but it really isn't. What it's actually inspired by is the Arkham Horror board game, which was inspired by the Call of Cthulhu roleplaying game, which actually WAS inspired by the works of HP Lovecraft...by this point in the chain the theme is not so much a veneer as a vague afterthought.

This is certainly worth the occasional play but it isn't a simplified version of Arkham Horror; it's essentially a clever but flavourless dice game with an Arkham style box lid.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Commenting on Solo game:

I have to say, I thoroughly enjoy playing this one solo.  It's a very light, luck-heavy dice rolling game in which you are matching dice to symbols on Adventure cards.  The rewards for matching these dice is sometimes "Elder Signs" of which a certain number are required to beat the game.

I really enjoy the simplicity of the game, but there are also lots of opportunities to break the rules with extra dice or rerolls using rewards you have earned from Adventure cards.  The only thing I don't like about the game is the rulebook, it has lots of holes and I recommend going to the FFG website to download the latest rulebook and FAQ files, I think you'll need them to play the game properly.

Definitely a nice one to keep in the collection for when you're home alone or just fancy a quick game by yourself.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
For anyone to enjoy this game, you have to realize a few things.  For starters, it's not an easy game - it will smack you around a lot.  Next, you have to realize that it is a dice game.  If you love dice, great!  If you seem to be consistently unlucky at dice rolls, this game will make you want to tear out your hair.

That being said, Elder Sign is a very fun game.  You play as pulp investigators trying to find clues, solve puzzles, and seal a gate before one of the ancient Cthulhu "Old Ones" enters the world and devours everything.  You accomplish this task by rolling dice and trying to match symbols that relate to the puzzle you are trying to conquer.  What these tasks reward you with varies from bonus items to Elder Signs, the keys that seal the gates.

The theme is definitely there in the cards, artwork, and feel of the game.  The only place the theme isn't the strongest would be rolling the dice.  The task at hand may ask for very thematic symbols, such as Lore or Investigation, but whether you feel that your investigator is investigating hard enough because you roll some dice is up to you.  I still love the challenge, the artwork/theme, and the tense gameplay.

Think of this game as King of Tokyo Puzzle, Cthulhu edition, but with very dire consequences.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
One solo play, plus a number of plays on the Android tablet version.

Nice cooperative dice game with Lovecraftian theme. 

It uses the Yahtzee mechanic (which is actually fine by me - Yahtzee's OK for what it is, albeit everyone round here seems to look down their nose at it) tweaked as per Knizia's excellent Risk Express (i.e. if you can't complete a line on the target card with your roll, you lose a dice before re-rolling) and puts some co-op mechanisms on top. You may not be able to overcome a challenge on your own turn, but you may be able to help someone else do it on theirs by banking a dice or two, or even by just being at the location to support them by holding a dice on their turn.

The art's pretty good in the FFG's usual slightly over the top way, which is fine for the theme. Some of the flavour text is a bit small for my aging eyes, plus as a lot of the spells and equipment boil down to roll an extra dice or preserve a life point you don't really feel you're in the middle of a horror story (I suspect you'd need some sort of RPG story telling element for that). However it does feel pretty tense when Cthulu (or his appointed chum in your game) is ahead and the end game is in sight...roll well!

RATING: 6.5
Very enjoyable game of throwing dices, and managing them. It all ultimately comes down to your dice roll, so I expected to hate this game somewhat but able to focus your dice, or hold on to one of your dice to your spell helped me mitigate the randomness somewhat. But I would have liked to see some greater degree of mitigation of randomness - then I would have taken away the charm from games such as this.

The flavor of Cthulu theme was not very strong indeed. I tried to read each of the cards, but nothing really truly felt epic. But I knew how it sacrificed theme to convert this to dice game, thus it did not bother me much.

For you get to control four investigators a turn in a solo game, it gets a bit tiresome. And while game did not feel to drag on unnecessarily, I was surprised to find out that almost an hour has passed from my very first play through.   Granted, this includes set-up and reading rules, so I can cut down maybe 10 mins, but for such a simple game, I expected a lot less than that (half an hour would have been sweet spot).

For how small the box size is, and unique dices that this game came with, this one is going to stay with me. I can see myself playing this whenever I have an urge to throw down dices, hoping to roll the hard six :).

RATING: 7
Elder Sign dishes out Lovecraftian gloom and menace in generous measure. It's terrific artwork contributes a lot to its ominous mood. Add in the fun that comes with dice rolling, and you've got a recipe for a pretty cool game. All that said, Elder Sign is the absolute definition of a "fiddly game". For a design of somewhat limited depth, it has an extraordinary number of bits to handle and adjustments to be made each turn. Some will find the requisite attention to these details tedious. Still, fans of Lovecraft and his particular brand of brooding dread are likely to find a lot in this game to enjoy and explore.

RATING: 8
This dice version of Arkham Horror retains a good deal of the flavor of its board game counterpart in a relatively quicker package. It's a decent tradeoff between the epic-ness of AH and a shorter playing time. My biggest problem with it is the ease of missing one or more fairly important rules at any given turn, and I doubt I've played a game where we haven't screwed up at least one fairly significant thing (forgetting to advance the clock, forgetting to draw and resolve a Mythos card at midnight, etc.) or neglected one or more key elements of our character (special powers, presence of clue tokens, availability of a key item) -- and this really hasn't been a problem for me with AH, probably due to the more deliberate pace of the latter.

Recent games have been with Unseen Forces (almost) fully integrated. With these options in, the game has more variety but also a much wider difficulty range, with some games being nigh impossible and others nearly suspenseless. Still, it's short enough that the variability isn't a deal breaker.

Looking forward to the Gates of Arkham expansion.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Number of players: 1-8

Components: (10)
Again, we're talking about Fantasty Flight Games. They always come through with component quality. This game is mostly cards and they're all of top quality. The custom dice are beautiful and easy to read.
  
Rules: (7)
FFG seem to consistently have the most poorly written rules in the industry, which is a real shame because they also produce some of the very best games. I feel as if whoever is writing the rules over there wants it to seem as if they're producing the most complex games in the history of the hobby. For the most part, this isn't true. They mostly produce beautiful games that have simple rules with terrible rule books.

Setup: (10)
Set-up is a snap. You'll lay down some exhibits (cards), sort out some other small cards and tokens and be read to go. 

Area required to play: (9)
You'll need enough room for six cards to be displayed (with space for one or two extra as the game progresses), and for a few decks to be set to one side along with a "clock" to keep track of turns and some various tokens. You'll also want to have some room in front of you for items that you've collected. I'm sure that most any table with accomidate this game.
 
Fun: (7)
I like this game a lot. I think that it's maybe a little too easy to win sometimes, but also a lot of that depends on how the dice roll. There is a good trade off in luck and decision making, however. You'll always have several rooms avaible to explore, and they'll all offer certain pros and cons that may benefit or hinder you in the short or long run.

Theme Integration: (5)
I cut this right down the middle. I really like Lovecraftian themes and this works for me. However, it could have be replaced by anything at all and would have worked the same way. It could have had a theme that wasn't as fun, and all in all I'm so glad that it has the theme that it does.


Replay Value: (10)
The random nature of what rooms come up, the dice, and the various "bosses" make this game very replayable. I also look forward to what they'll do if (when) they release some expansions.

Storage: (8)
I ended up tossing the insert. The box is very small, but it holds everything nicely. Maybe you'll need to invest in some plastic baggies.

Accessibility: (9)
This game is easy to teach and easy to play.

Over-All/Bonuses/Biases: Cthulhu fhtagn! Ia!
