RATING: 3
After my 2nd play of this game and a few digital plays of the app, I've come to the conclusion that I just don't like this game. I like dice rolling and I don't mind some randomness, but the dice rolling never seems very fun (compare to King of Tokyo) and decisions don't seem very meaningful. If feels more like the game is playing you. And, even at 4 people this game is a bit of a slog. There's nothing to do when it's not your turn and what's happening a person's turn is generally not very interesting to you. I could never imagine playing this with more than 4 people and I could possibly be talked into to playing this at 2-3 players, but even then I think I could find something more fun to play. A lot of people seem to like this game, so I must be missing something.

RATING: 7.5
Based in the Lovecraft universe, players roll dice to investigate rooms to get items, other world cards, or elder signs. Players use elder signs to seal in the "Ancient one"- a terrible monster. The goal is to seal in the monster before he is released. If the monster is released, he attacks and its almost guaranteed that you will lose. 

Fun dice chucking game. Some subtle rules that are easily forgotten, but the more you play the more rules you ll remember.

RATING: 7
Elder Sign is a fast-paced, cooperative dice game of supernatural intrigue for one to eight players by Richard Launius and Kevin Wilson, the designers of Arkham Horror. Players take the roles of investigators racing against time to stave off the imminent return of the Ancient One. Armed with tools, allies, and occult knowledge, investigators must put their sanity and stamina to the test as they adventure to locate Elder Signs, the eldritch symbols used to seal away the Ancient Ones and win the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I like the idea of having an Arkham horror dice game. There was Arkham express that followed the same idea but that simply failed to be a good game.

Still, I think that there is a few things lacking in elder sign that does not make it a perfect game.

The biggest problem is the paper weight characters. Most of the strategy of the game is to use your equipment wisely to fulfill quests that are going to give you additional equipment. But if you have no equipment, then you cannot succeed anything. Since all items are one time use, you will eventually run out of items.

In order to partially solve this, a good suggestion I made is to roll 2 green dice when searching the lost and found and keeping one of the dice.

The second problem is that the strategy is pretty low. Like I said, most of the strategy comes from which item I should use and which quest I should fulfill. When you are on a quest, the only strategy left is which task are you going to fulfill before another task and sometimes you are forced to do certain task first. 

So compared to other express dice game, like Dune Express, there is not much strategy in which dice you are going to keep over the dice you want to re-roll.

I don't like the design of the dice instead of 3-1-1-1 faces where 3 have numbered faces from 1-3, I would have used a 3-2-1 model, so that there are different odds for the 2 last symbols. Right now, skulls, scrolls and Terror have the same odds to appear.

The rolls required to win does not make sense either. Why do I need 3 terror face to complete this quest?

In Arkham Express, the dice system was awesome because each face allowed you to gain items or clues and you could push your luck to change the stuff you get, but the more you rolled, the more you had a chance to fall on an encounter face which gets locked once rolled.

But elder sign does not have the same feeling at all, it does not have the feeling of risk and fear when rolling dice which you have in Arkham Express.

UPDATE: After playing the app for a many games, sure this game is pretty abstract. The die faces and the actions you are doing does not thematically make sense, but the game is still relatively good. The first expansion fixes a few things like the souvenir and a few mission cards shop while adding the blessed condition.

Another advantage of this game is that you can play rapidly with almost anybody within an hour. The dice mechanics is not obvious first and they might not have the necessary experience to play the game accurately, but it can be done. My only regrets is that the app takes so little time to setup and plays so much faster, that I prefer the app to pulling out the game on the table, especially for solo play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The Arkham Horror game doesn't call me.  I am wondering if it was the novel theme of Lovecraftian world or the game mechanisms.  Elder Sign and its mobile game adaptation Elder Sign: Omen appear to be more streamlined than the Arkham Horror game. Matching glyphs in the adventures seems to be testing the player's conductive and deductive abilities at the same time.  It's like finding the right keys to unlock the next level.  There are 16 characters to choose from to form a group of 4 adventurers each time.  The different combinations of characters would yield different approach and strategy to tackle the problems.  A simple combination calculation resolve that there would be 1820 combinations of characters in the makeup of the group you selected.  The random glyphs you get from the book removes the possibility of a math game.  The ultimate objective is to find the sufficient no. of elder signs to seal off the gate from which the "ancient" monsters emerge.  The characters have special abilities that can help the group, plus the artifacts they gained after successfully completing an adventure. On the other hand, I always doubt, in this kind of game, that if winning the game really requires your own mettle and intelligence to construct a workable strategy or pure luck to resolve the case.  It is a popular game certainly though. As a wargamer, it seems to be better than some of the linear plots of those Victory Point Games, say, the State of Siege series.

RATING: 7
Fun little dice game with some Arkham Horror flavor. It's faster to set up and play than its older brother, but it also has the capacity to drag out much longer than its older brother due to a more random way of acquiring doom tokens and the simple fact that dice rolls are the only resolution mechanic. There is some tactical decision-making to be done here, but it can be hobbled easily by a string of bad rolls or bad card draws, and the random doom token generation means that you can't even be sure you'll die to the claws of an Ancient One any time soon.

RATING: 6
In theme with hopelessness due to inherent randomness of die rolling. This is the best thing about this game, to generate such feeling of desperation. 

I dont think that what I get from this game is enjoyment. It's an intense arm wrestling with fate with a dark theme at that to make you go insane or laugh at how worse could it get and how tough could your luck be.

However, luck factors can be minimised with careful planning and strategies with numbers of investigators.

It plays nice and fast ,easy to learn yet hard to beat, a perfect way to pass the time too.

Only played this game solo or duo. I dont dare to introduce this to my playing group. They will not be happy with how a game can randomly make you lose in a flip of some combination of cards out of no where.

The game is uncaring at best but that precious feeling when victory is earned... priceless

I would like to note the replayability of this game where I found it to be different everytime. However, I'm not the sort of player who read the same book twice, hence, never replay the beaten Ancient Ones. This may change if I can find a group that can tolerate and can be bothered to have their precious time be potentially wasted at any point in the game.

Life is harsh and it will squeeze you every angle possible.
This game is a brutal reminder of such facts...

I keep coming back to torture myself with this game only because... to win against fate is one's life achievement in itself!

so you might want to ask yourself before buying this game or any Arkham Horror, Eldritch Horror etc. if your real life is already enough an intense game of fate to your liking.

RATING: 8
Read the rules. Storing dice on either spells or other players is extremely important. Without using this mechanic some tasks may appear impossible. Remember it's a cooperative game. Just because the first person to try fails, does not mean the next person will, given a hand with stored dice. Scrolls for instance. 
There are dice in this game. It does have a random element. It is a cooperative game. It is in the Cthulu setting. If those things don't attract you, move on. Plenty of other games out there. All those things work for me. Fun short dip. Some people think this is long with too much down time. WTF? The turns should be fast. Play with a timer or something because your fellow players must be taking it way too serious.

RATING: 6
Essentially, this is Arkham Horror lite. My chief criticism of Arkham Horror is that the game is so fiddly that it would have benefitted from being a 1 vs. many rather than a co-op (a la Middle Earth Quest). Elder Sign remains a pure co-op, but it benefits from significantly streamlined gameplay.

The mechanics of this game are solid, if a little uninspired. This is a problem inherent in dice games I think; there's really only so many ways to dress up Yahtzee's "roll some dice, set some aside, and re-roll for a better score" mechanic. Nevertheless, there's enough going on in terms of gameplay to keep the game interesting, and even so, Elder Sign has such a rich theme that it's worth playing for that alone.

RATING: N/A
Elder Sign is a fast-paced, cooperative dice game of supernatural intrigue for one to eight players by Richard Launius and Kevin Wilson, the designers of Arkham Horror. Players take the roles of investigators racing against time to stave off the imminent return of the Ancient One. Armed with tools, allies, and occult knowledge, investigators must put their sanity and stamina to the test as they adventure to locate Elder Signs, the eldritch symbols used to seal away the Ancient Ones and win the game.

RATING: 7
This is an astounding condensation and concentration of the core challenges and themes of Arkham Horror into a dice game. It also appears to be quite a challenge, unless fate hated us more than usual and/or we got some crucial rule wrong. Which is entirely possible, I’m sad to say, because the rules are an unwelcome throwback to FFG’s encyclopaedic style that describes every possible situation in detail, except for the one you’re interested in.

Shame, because the game is not that complicated, and there are few instances where you have to look up anything once you properly get rolling. With a gallery of a gazillion Lovecraftian illustrations at hand, it’s not surprising that everything looks swell, so it’s all the more worthwhile to mention that there is also some very nice flavor text on just about everything – monsters, quests and so on.

All in all, a very enjoyable pastime, and if I’d like co-ops more, I’d probably love this one.

RATING: 7.5
Definitely very close to being too long for the type of decisions being made in the game.  Almost every game has me feeling a bit of fatigue from doing the same actions over and over by 3/4 of the way through the game.  Start wondering how much longer until it is over.  First 3/4 of the game is enjoyable, though.

-evaluating which location you should attempt this turn
-pushing your luck a bit
-gaining gear that helps mitigate the luck in the game  

Now, somebody needs to design a game that uses the same dice/card mechanisms as ES, but plays in only 45-60 mins. Age of War is too light and doesn't have any gear.  
Ancient Terrible Things felt sort of ES-ish, but I still preferred how the cards are set up in ES.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Elder Sign looks amazing, it's a blast to play, and it actually feels like Call of Cthulhu -- the mood is excellent, and the play experience is improved if everyone gets into it at least a bit (which we did). I can also see Alysia liking it, which is a big plus.

After our first play, it seemed too easy -- but we were playing it wrong, letting investigators live even if health or sanity was at zero. So for our second play, we upped the difficulty by implementing three of the designers' suggestions: even monster distribution, advancing the clock by 4 hours instead of 3, and rolling a green die at midnight and adding a doom token on any investigation result. I realized my mistake re: health/sanity midway through, and even that major flub in our favor couldn't save us from the upped difficulty.

For play three, we went back to vanilla except for even monster distribution and it ran just fine. No one got devoured, but the doom track was at 6/10 and we had a monster on every adventure when we pulled it out. I can see it feeling a bit too easy after a few more plays (though I could be wrong), but there are lots of tweaks available if that proves to be the case.

I'd heard that the rules were a bit of a mess, but I didn't find that to be the case; it's a nice clear rulebook, and nothing tripped us up. (I often miss a rule or two the first time out, regardless of the game!) The only real downside I see is that fighting the GOO is pretty boring; I'd almost rather just lose if the doom track fills up. That's a pretty minor complaint, though.

Elder Sign is just plain fun to play. It delivers on the theme, mood, and enjoyment factor I was looking for, and is more immersive than I expected. This is well on its way to becoming one of my favorite co-op games.

Its a co-op version of Yahtzee with monsters and that is much more fun than I'd have thought!

RATING: 6
Elder Sign was my only foray into the Cthulhu universe.  There's no way I was going to spend several hours of my life playing any of the other games; looking at you Arkham Horror.  I heard this was shorter, and lighter, and co-op with a single player variant, so I picked it up.  

In the game you are basically trying to roll symbol combinations that are depicted on various cards, which represent rooms.  If you do that successfully, you defeat the monster inside, or close the room off to bad things, etc.  If you don't do it successfully, then more bad things happen, such as more monsters arriving, or your character getting injured in some way.

Two things struck me immediately about Elder Sign when I played.  The first was that it is very repetitive.  You just keep rolling those dice over, and over, and over again.  Secondly, though much shorter than other Cthulhu themed games, it's still pretty long for what it is.  After a couple plays I just couldn't bring myself to go through it again.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
3rd best game of 2011.
Don't have time to play Arkham Horror? Well, this won't solve that problem. Go to Eldritch Horror for that.. Elder Sign draws from same Lovecraftian mythos, but it's NOT a rpg-lite story-driven horror game. What is it then? It's one hour or awesome action-packed dice-chucking fun. Theme does come through enough for it to be exciting. It's not as cerebral as some euro co-ops (this is about step below Ghost Stories), making it perfect 'beer&pretzel game'. If you love exciting dicerolls, this is like best thing ever. Highly recommended.

2-Player Comment:
Works well with two too. I'd say best player counts are 2 and 3 followed by 4. 5 is ok. It's 6+p game in name only, too much downtime.

Expansions:
+Elder Sign: Unseen Forces
+Elder Sign: Gates of Arkham
+Elder Sign: Grave Consequences

RATING: 8
well, I enjoy this game immensely. Of course you'd expect me to be predisposed toward it given that [gameid=15987] is my favourite game. However, this is not AH lite, not at all. Sure the theme is the same, but it doesn't quite tell the story that AH does. It does, however, play very well with the full complement of 8 players, something AH does not. When solo, if you can't get extra dice early then you are screwed. It doesn't matter whether they are Red, Yellow or White, you need those extra dice. The Investigator's Special Ability can make all the difference when solo as you get to use it so frequently.

RATING: 9
Picked this up for cheap, as a way to ease into the whole Cthulhu-thing, what with Arkham & Eldritch Horror. They seem to have a lot of stuff going on, and as I play mostly solo, the setup time is critical for me - I quickly lose interest if the initial setup is taking too long, or if it's a big hassle to reset after a game. Robinson falls a bit for that, but this doesn't have that problem - it's easily setup and you'll be playing within five minutes.

The game is tons of fun, too, although, one could argue that it's pretty easy for a Cthulhu-themed game. Rarely do you get a tense experience, and the endings can be very anti-climax when it's possible to buy the Elder Signs which wins the game - 9 games out of 10 you'll be hoarding trophies to get what's needed to buy one, and the last turn you just buy the signs to seal the elder away. I've heard Unseen Forces changes this, and it's on my list of games to get.

The game has some luck involved, of course, but the thing is, you need to mitigate the luck factor by playing good, leveraging all possible advantages you may have got.

All in all, the theme is great, the artwork is outstanding and if you like to chuck some dice at your leisure, this game is for you.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[microbadge=1714]

[u]20-Aug-2015[/u]:  This is a dice game based in the Cthulhu mythos.  A number of investigators move from one adventure card to another trying to resolve tasks by matching dice results as listed on each card.  The players must acquire enough Elder Signs through succeeding at these adventures to destroy the Ancient One.  Otherwise, the big bad will awaken and most likely, devour everyone still in the game.

While the base game is rather simple and generally on the lower side of the difficulty scale, The Gates of Arkham expansion brings a ton of stuff to the table.  There are several new mechanisms, an entirely new set of adventure and mythos cards, new Ancient Ones, a much stronger cohesive narrative and flow of gameplay, and oh yeah…it’s hard!
 
The Base game and the Gates expansion seem like two ends of the spectrum in terms of difficulty and complexity.  Base is fairly easy.  Gates is pretty difficult.  Base has a simple ruleset without much extra "stuff."  But Gates has a lot more going on, many more actions, modifiers, and interactions between cards.  They almost feel like two different games.

Right now, I feel as though I want this game to fall somewhere in the middle.  While faster playing, there isn't much thinking required playing just the Base game.  And even though I enjoy the higher interaction and enhanced experience of the Gates expansion, I think it may become frustrating for me sooner rather than later.

With that being said, The Gates expansion is a must own for this game, IMO.  It adds a [b]ton[/b] to the game in every sense of the word - challenge, components, narrative.  It really does have it all.  Overall, Elder Sign is pretty much what I wanted after playing Eldritch Horror.  It’s smaller in physical presence, game time, and narrative scope.  The theme is still not my thing, though.

I think the Gates expansion is far and above a better thematic experience than the base game, but I really didn’t pay much attention to it.  I read the flavor text of the cards, and that’s about all I got in terms of a story.  But what I do get is that tension and feel of desperation as more of the bad stuff comes out and gets in your way.  So, while I couldn’t tell you a story about my session, I can tell you it [i]felt[/i] like a story.

To my surprise, I’ve really enjoyed my plays of this so far, and I look forward to finding the “right mix” of the two experiences I had with this game.

I hear the app is also great, but the board game just makes me want to play it more.

RATING: 6
First impression was pretty good. It's a nice, light co-op game and I love the artwork and theme (which is very pasted on). It's essentially Arkham Horror Yahtzee, but I'm okay with that.

Too easy!

We houseruled it thusly: when the clock strikes midnight, if there is no doom counter above the Ancient One, place one there. If a doom counter is already there, add it to the doom track. 

This seems to put the balance where I like it - the game is tense and difficult without being impossible or too long.

RATING: 8
I struggle with rating this game, but not because of any specific flaws.  It is beautifully designed, both functionally and in terms of artwork; it leverages a fantastic theme (though perhaps not as robustly as it could); it does a nice job of guarding against player quarterbacking, the bane of all co-op games.  Add in a challenging objective, easily scalable difficulty, and a seamless transition between co-op and solo play, and what's not to love?

Well, nothing really.  It's a great game!  But the Gates of Arkham expansion is so good, and so profoundly reworks and improves on the base game, that I can't imagine playing regular Elder Sign again.  If Gates of Arkham didn't exist, Elder Sign would be a regular favorite.  With Gates of Arkham at hand, most of the original game is relegated to a quiet but respectful respite on the shelf.

RATING: 4

That being said, I am giving it a +1 bonus to rating solely because of the Cthulhu theme. I love the theme plain and simple.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Elder Sign seems to have been designed for those who consider Arkham Horror to be too long and fiddly. It uses the same theme and follows a similar objective overview, but plays as a simple cooperative dice game rather then AH's more in depth adventure horror game.

Its nicely enough presented (even if its art is copied almost entirely from AH) and the quick, easy play even appeals to me -an avid AH fan- from time to time (there's no denying that is quicker to play and easier to get to the table). The problem is its been boiled down so much there's very little left to really feel, and you could interchange 100 themes onto this game without notice.

The lavish Lovecraft inspired art is neutralised by the simplistic and abstract dice rolling, and along with it much of the dark and foreboding feeling of suspense that comes from titles such as Arkham Horror and Mansions of Madness.

It also appears very easy- we've trashed the game a couple of times without barely breaking a sweat (the doom track not even half full both times). This only adds to the feeling of playing a woefully neutered version of AH. I'd rather achieve a hard earned victory once every 10 games then sail to an easy win every time I play.

People are lauding Elder Sign as 'Quick Play Arkham Horror' and they are wrong, this is comparatively just a light and generic dice game themed in the Arkham universe. It shares non of Arkham's weight, difficulty or thrill.

Doubt rating of 7 will maintain unless more plays reveal the easy wins to be a fluke..

Update- it didn't. 4 games, 4 wins, easy as pie. I've trawled the rules and FAQs looking for something we are doing wrong that's making it easier then it should be but there is nothing, it really is just that easy.

Additional Note- I also now have [i]Elder Sign Omens[/i], the digital version of Elder Sign on my phone and its much better! Amongst other things it has AO specific monsters, adventures and Mythos cards which saves much of the theme, and it also steps up the difficulty with harsher penalties and mythos as well as perma-death to the investigators (no respawn when you die). This makes the digital game trump the base Elder Sign hands down in all areas accept player capacity (it only goes to 4), and I'd rate it higher as a result.

Progressive rating: 7-6
(8 for [i]Elder Sign Omens[/i])

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Arkham Horror definitely provides more ambiance.  It is the slowly developing symphony (with the right group, and just a few of the expansions thrown in).  However, it takes a long time to set up, and its fiddly.

Elder Sign is a very quick set up.  Games can be played in just over an hour.  The rules are pretty straight forward, and there's just enough theme to get the job done.  Not a particularly difficult game...but that's all right because it means that it can be played with a larger range of people.

There's discussion about whether this is just a glorified "Yahtzee."  I did not find this to be the case, unless one is also going to start claiming that Dominant Species is, say, a glorified Agricola, which is a glorified Stone Age, etc.  Yes, you roll dice, and are attempting to get particular combinations.  That is the core mechanic.  There is a push your luck mechanic, too, similar to, say, Farkle.  But there are enough twists to to the dice mechanic to make the game it's own beast: spells that allow dice to be set aside, items that allow additional dice, effects that "lock up" dice, monsters that require additional dice combinations.  All of these thematic "conditionings" of the dice mechanic, make Elder Sign feel unique.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
In the world of Arkham Horror, players are investigators, working cooperatively to destroy the Ancient One. The main mechanic in this game is rolling 6 dice (of which spells can add more dice, or allow you to re-roll) to complete tasks, Yahtzee style. Failing tasks generally affects your sanity and stamina, while being successful allows you to gain items, such as Elder Signs, which a certain number are needd to dispatch the Ancient One. The Ancient One will awaken if enough doom markers are placed on it, which it gains from investigators dying, or failing tasks. When the Ancient One awakens, you might have a chance to try and fight it before he devours you.

The dice do add a good deal of luck, and some adventure cards are much tougher than others. Worth a look if you are an Arkham Horror fan. It's reasonably fun, though it may bog down with more players as you wait for your turn. But you have to enjoy the dice aspect of the game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Thing is, I do have a place for fun games. Where deep doesn't really matter (AH, LNoE etc) but this just isn't clicking with me.

Maybe this will change with a few more plays...

RATING: 9
Love it. Great quick Dice game!

I prefer this to Arkham Horror based on everything I know. Usually for a game to be mechanically simple on this level, it also loses theme and becomes less flavorful. Elder Sign is a rare game that manages to be extremely simple and easy (without being brainless) yet is still completely full of theme and atmosphere. It's difficult to pull off and it makes this game appealing more often than many lighter euro games which take about the same time/simplicity but have less theme.

RATING: 8
Elder sign is a dice rolling game that is high on theme but low on strategy.  This is probably what most folks would term ameritrash.  I find it to be a lot of fun.  Players work together to gather elder signs in order to seal away the elder god before he is unleashed and destroys the world.  The game seems to be a bit on the easy side.  We have yet to lose.  Decisions come down to whether or not your character can afford to take on an adventure, and how many dice are available vs. required to complete an adventure.  Once that is decided it is simple dice rolling luck to see if you succeed.  There is a bit of suspense on each turn as the dice are rolled, but overall there is very little tension building, especially given our win record.  The game needs something more to create tension and thus bring it to our table more often.  For now, I prefer the electronic version Elder Sign: Omens.

RATING: 5
I really wanted to like Elder Sign. I love the theme, I love the era, I love the artwork, I love the flavor text, but somehow all that just isn't enough.

The problem for me is dice-rolling. Yeah, there are decisions to be made, but each dice roll just feels like another pull on an H.P. Lovecraft slot-machine. Elder Sign is easy to teach and to play because it is basically Cthulhu Yahtzee.

The cooperative nature of the game is almost nonexistent as there is little interaction between players. On the bright side, that means the game plays just as well solo as with others. Warning: Due to how the clock works, Elder Sign shouldn't be attempted with 5 or more players.

From a design standpoint, all the fiddly little tokens were a poor decision in a game with the potential for dice to bounce across the playing area. Spinners like in King Of Tokyo should have been used for player's sanity and stamina and for the enemy's Doom and Elder Signs. Plus, they would have cut down on set-up time in a game that takes 2 hours to play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
There are four levels of Cthulhu action that FFG makes available to folks: a living card game (solid but WAY too complex for casual gamers), Arkham Horror (an adventure game for people with 5+ hrs to spend), Eldritch Horror (for people who wish Arkham Horror was shorter)... and Elder Sign, the best-of-show that adds all the flavor and reduces complexity to virtually zero.  (We shall not speak of Mansions of Madness.)

If you've played any recent dice game, you'll recognize Elder Sign's core.  Prevent the Old Ones from coming into our world, or die trying.

If there's any issue to this game, it's that the "co-op" feel is thin.  You're all on the same page but there's little bonafide interaction unless you share the same space, which only generally happens if someone failed an adventure.  Also, many of the items are thematically compelling but mechanically the same in regard to bonuses.  If you can overlook these issues, you'll have fun with Elder Sign.

Otherwise, honestly, just play Call (or Trail) of Cthulhu.  You'll be happier that way.

RATING: 9
Le signe des anciens est grosso modo une version 'light' des autres jeux Horreur à Arkham (Les contrées, etc.). En revanche la thématique et l'ambiance sont là. Que l'on soit fan déjà du culte de Cthulhu ou que l'on souhaite découvrir (je trouve que l'aspect coopératif du jeu est très bien pour faire découvrir justement), ce jeu est très facile à sortir. La mise en place est relativement rapide et une fois la partie lancée, le stress est de mise :D. Il arrive fréquemment que l'on hurle soit de plaisir (tous ensemble en plus) sur un ultime jet de dé réussi ou, à l'inverse un échec cuisant qui va nous rendre la tâche encore plus difficile! Pour arriver à clouer le bec à ces grands anciens, il va falloir coopérer en bonne intelligence et calculer les coups à venir en fonction des capactités de chaque investigateurs, des aventures présentes, des malus du grand ancien à affronter et le meilleur pour la fin : les fameuses cartes "Mythe" qui apporte son lot d'évènements parfois assez destructeurs. Pour moi c'est un jeu incontournable. Je l'ai pris avec sa première extension Forces Occultes qui, je pense, une extension qui est devenue indispensable car elle rééquilibre pas mal de règles qui donne au jeu encore plus de plaisirs :-)

RATING: 7.5
In the museum a great old one is on the verge of awakening and you have to prevent this from happening. How you do that: collecting enough Elder signs in Adventures. The Game has really cool mechanics, using dice in order to solve adventures. The adventure cards become trophies you can use in order to heal, buy stuff or defeat monsters. Also you get rewards for mastering the adventures. These include the much needed elder signs. 

I really like the mechanis, with rolling the dice and forwarding the clock. The components are really cool and the whole game is small enough to take with you on a holiday (unlike Eldritch Horror). On the downside the game is easily beat, a problem solved by adding the expansions.

Could this game be more intense than AH? When I play this game sweat drips down my brow and I barely speak a word for the full game. I was thinking when I purchased this game that it was going to be a medium to medium light dice fest with an AH theme. Boy was I wrong! This game has all the intensity and I would say the length of game play that AH has...just fewer components and more table space. Don't get me wrong...I like it...I like it alot. It is still very difficult to beat.

This will never be a substitute for AH for me though. I do feel the stories and events you read about as you play AH definitely make the experience for me. Perhaps those stories also temper the extreme intensity of trying to make great die rolls or be devoured...this is what feels to be the nature of Elder Sign. Both games are fun to play and have their own time and place to be played.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Arguably the most beautifully worked theme for Yahtzee ever produced. Reveal 6 locations from the deck, each location has a series of combination sets you need to complete (some in a specific order) with your dice. Each successful roll which completes one of the sets in a location's series is locked away, reducing the dice you get to roll towards the next set. Each failure loses you one die for the next roll, but you do have the option to lock 1 die in if you want. All series must complete within the one player's turn to be successful. Each room has different penalties for failure (the inevitable Cthulhu loss of sanity and health) and rewards for success (elder sign tokens, clue tokens, which allow re-rolls, plus the familiarly based skill cards such as weapons, skills, spells and allies, which mostly provide dice addition and manipulation abilities), and draw a new location card once done. Anyway, keep going until you're done - you need a bunch elder sign tokens before the turn based timer completes, with an event card mixing things up every 4 turns. So all the good stuff in a good dice game is there, plus great theme. The only reason I haven't rated it higher is that the game simply goes too long for what is essentially just a roll-fest, where the major decision each turn is whether to use up a clue token to re-roll. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
"Not terrible, but ultimately it's too long for the level of randomness, or too random for the length. The postage-stamp monster images that you put face-down don't help the theme. The flavor text font is unreadable."

What I like:
- Pure cooperative game
- Cool dice
- Reasonable weight and complexity

What I don't like:
- The sense of frustration if you FAIL a lot of tasks
- There is very little actual cooperation:
  - "Assisting" other players is a [b]very[/b] weak action
  - No way to trade items or trophies
- Can run long. Would be best at 30-45 minutes, but can go 2 hours

It's a good co-op, but not one of my favorites. With most co-ops, you are continually making a little progress. Perhaps not as much as you wanted, and there may be setbacks, but it is fluid. In Elder Sign, there is a very discrete SUCCEED/FAIL status on each task and each adventure. We had a long series of failures in our first game, with nothing we could do about it. That was demoralizing.

For whatever reason, other "move around and complete dice challenge" games (like Star Trek: Expeditions and Exalted: Legacy of the Unconquered Sun) don't feel punishing like this one.

I think my initial rating was a 5 or 6. Then it went up as high as a solid 7. Now it's back down. 

I would put the weight at 2.5, a bit higher than the current BGG-voted value. Based on several plays of ES and several of Witch of Salem, my wife and I both prefer WoS as a light Lovecraft-themed game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A nice, accessible coop with the general theme of Arkham Horror but less complexity.  The game plays easily enough and it is easy to both teach and learn.  The way that the game intertwines challenges in the museum with those in the outer worlds is a nice twist, and gives the players lots of options.

Elder sign also does a good job of getting difficulty right.  Sure, you can occasionally have games where it feels like either the players or the Old One are just cruising along in unstoppable fashion, but those are pretty rare.  The game is often a nail-biter with the outcome determined just the way you'd want to see it if this were a movie.

If there's one thing that can get out of control in-game, it's selecting the characters players will use.  Although they are generally balanced, some combinations simply have far, far more utility than others.  Once you figure those out, the game can become easier than it should be.  However, that's easy to fix by randomizing character selection to some extent so that you can't build a "dream team" every time you play.

RATING: 6.5

Yet another cooperative game. Game is fun but not as challenging as other cooperative titles like Ghost Stories or Yggdrasil where you can differ the difficulty level. Elder Sign has only one level of difficulty which is not really hard. Generally most of the games I've played were wins.

Also the mechanism of the game is very repeatable. It's generally chosing one adventure, rolling dices to solve the adventure with risk managment thanks to used objects. That's generally it. It's a simple mechanism for a simple dice game but included in 60+ minutes game and this might make the game a bit boring especially if you're lucky and there is no real threat of loosing the game.

Although the game has mentioned disadvantages, it has also one big advantage over other cooperative games as it might be played with 8 people what is a lot for cooperative game.

There also seems to be a great potential for expansion.

Thank you Fantasy Flight.

RATING: 9.2
This game was quite an eye opener when we first played. The theme and the layout alongside the objectives and the characters creates a real immersive game. Some say its too random with the dice. Rolling and adding bonuses to overcome monsters and spirits. Its really quite a smart design. Even the shape of the dice are pleasing to the eye. The events in the game are solid too. It has a distinct  presence of pressure that it puts onto players and really helps to create the atmosphere of fear and dread. This is an easy game to learn and the mechanics are simple enough too using cards as boosters for extra dice is a nice asset in the game. Tokens earned from successes and investigation bonuses. We cant praise this game enough. It stands out above many games because it has it all. A solid thematic experience great artwork and a storyline too. The Lovecraft horror manifestation in board games has really added a quite unique horror experience. Something that we have enjoyed. Even the kids. My 12 yr old daughter chooses this quite often as her first play.

RATING: N/A
When is Fantasy Flight going to craft a half decent rulebook? 

The seven page re-write of the rules in this game's file section on the Geek are better and more usable than the rules that come in the box, while in addition being shorter and more concise.  

Fantasy Flight: Stop making people skip around the rulebook to find the info they need. Stop burying important rules in some paragraph in a tangentially related section of the rules.


This game is not so much easy as it is really swingy.  The balance is just kind of off. I you have a little bad luck you can get really hosed, but you have to have some bad luck for the difficulty to ramp up.  If you do reasonably well rolling for what you need, you will win easily.  The more players there are, the easier things get, I feel.  

The item cards are just not thematic at all in this game. Laughably so.  I don't really care, but it just goes to show that Ameritrash games can have really pasted on themes.  

All in all, I'm kind of disappointed in this game. I was pretty psyched for a streamlined version of Arkham Horror and fun dice game.  Not sure that this game is either of those.  I'm going to need to play it a few more times to make sure how I feel about the game, but it's not looking good so far.

RATING: 8
If you expect epic adventures, you will be sorely disappointed. "Elder Sign" is a bit meatier dice rolling game with just a touch of theme. It doesn't tell a story, but it allows you to kill a few monsters and kick the ass of some ugly Ancient God in a much shorter time than the sprawling thematic games like AH or EH. It's a fun, wild ride, maybe a bit on the easier side (at least without the expansion), but it still offers strategic choices and allows you to have fun in a cooperative game with a bunch of friends. I rate it highly for its simplicity and straightforwardness, which allows me to play it with my 5 years old daughter. All in all, a very good game for what it tries to achieve.

RATING: 6
A fun fast alternative to Arkham Horror. Easy to setup and teach to new gamers. Great as a filler between more serious games. The artwork and components are nice. I expected all of the art to be recycled from past AH games, but that wasn't the case.

My complaints about the game-
1. It's almost entirely based around luck. There are strategic choices to make about which dice to keep, but once you're on your 2nd or 3rd game of Elder Sign, these choices are so obvious I'd hardly call it "strategy".

2. The game is too easy. There's a lot of potential to fix this with future expansions, but as of now there's just not much challenge.

RATING: 7.3

Solo Player Value = Excellent

Two Player Value = Excellent

Three Player Value = Excellent but more difficult with more players.


Elder Sign to me is Arkham Horror light, or Arkham Horror version 2.0. I think that is a good thing.

Elder Sign is a pure dice game form of Arkham Horror. Players use dice to power everything in the game. However, the game is controlled through cards.

Elder Sign uses essentially the same game play as Arkham Horror. Players are still trying to stop an evil Ancient One from destroying the world. Players still travel to various locations to earn Elder Signs to help defeat the Ancient One. Players still earn various items to help them on their adventure. Monsters still pop up to thwart the adventures and must be dealt with.

The major difference with Elder Sign is that players use dice at the locations to accomplish pre-set tasks in a push-your-luck mechanic. Items provide players more dice to use. Accomplishing a task earns the player rewards, like Elder Signs and items, to help defeat the Ancient One. Failing a task damages the player.

I like the push-your-luck mechanic. I think it fits nicely into the Arkham Horror universe.

The artwork and components are well done.

The set-up time of Elder Sign is minimal. Full set-up takes only a few minutes. This is in contrast to Arkham horror where set-up is enormous.

Play time is also great reduced from Arkham Horror. Elder Sign can usually be set-up, played and cleaned up within an hour. 

The difficulty level of Elder Sign is a little suspect though. In fact, many would simply call the game too easy. The tasks at each location are easily beaten. Elder Signs are easy to obtain. Defeating the Ancient One is usually quick and painless. Without a strong challenge the game becomes dull and boring. However, by using a few alternate rules the difficulty level can be easily adjusted to make the game more difficult.


Pros - 
- Great push-your-luck dice mechanic
- Good Arkham Horror feeling
- Quick set-up and play time

Cons -
- Too easy difficulty


Overall Playability = 7.0

Design = 8
Strategy = 7
Luck = 8
Artwork & Components = 6
Use of Mechanics = 8
Time of Play = 7
Fun = 8
Innovation = 6
Analysis Paralysis = 6
Theme = 6


[b]-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------[/b]


Here is will discuss the Elder Sign expansion [thing=137479][/thing].

Unseen Forces goes a long way toward correcting the small flaws in the base game.  It also adds a few extra pieces to help round out the game and complete the Arkham Horror feeling.

Overall, unseen Forces raises the difficulty level of the base game in many way.  Many new location cards have been added to the game effectively doubling the number of locations.  Most of these new locations are rough and greatly increase the difficulty of the game.  

New Midnight cards have been added as well.  The new Midnight cards are of extreme difficulty.  Playing with these mean almost certain doom and are only for the well seasoned player.

The entrance has changed with this expansion.  Players can no longer buy elder signs.  This helps increase the games difficulty.  New entrance abilities have been added and the players now have new options while at the entrance.

A Cursed die and Blessed die have also been added to the game.  This is a nice touch and helps round out the Arkham Horror experience.

Unseen Forces changes the base game enough to warrant a new scoring of the game.

RATING: 3
It feels like the only real decision you make in this game is which location to go, and once you do that you just have to roll the dice and hope you match everything that's on that card's location, sometimes spending an item or clue to add a die or reroll.

As a result, the game feels less interesting than the Yahtzee game it got its dice mechanics from (since you could at least decide on different things to go after based on what you rolled), but has this lack of agency hidden behind all this extra rules and cruft in the name of making the game seem cool and thematic.

I'd much rather play a game like King of Tokyo where you can actually go for different results that are all viable, then this 'roll the dice and hope it matches' garbage. I've given this game a chance twice now, had really poor experiences both times, and I doubt I'll give it another.

RATING: N/A
[q=""]I don't think the intent was to allow the piling of all spare monsters on a useless adventure.[/q]

Only played it once, but if you have an investigator with a high stamina, if you pile the monsters on an adventure that has a single stamina penalty, you can essentially use the monster pile to get trophies. I found this useful when the other adventures had a sanity penalty, and my investigator was down to one sanity.

Also, if you pile monsters onto an adventure and don't clean them out, that increases the chances of the Warlock, who freezes a red die (and returns to the cup when defeated), of coming out. So I think the design is that you must eventually clear out the monsters. How soon is up to you.

RATING: 2
See symbols in rows, roll dice, if dice match symbol in one row, place dice, if not lose one die and re-roll (too bad if you match all symbols in one roll, the game forces a re-roll per row).

Sometimes you make it (get cards/tokens to help move towards the game end), sometimes you don't (get bored, pass dice, wait a seemingly interminable age for them to come round again).

I've no idea why this is a game, there's just nothing to it, it's not even push-your-luck, rather do-or-do-not as there is no decision making going on.

Production is excellent but overly fiddly, the theme is such a paste job I could only smell the glue, not the fear.

Played twice (with months between plays), just to confirm my first impressions, I won't be playing a third.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I have to check the rules to ensure we played everything right, because it was so damn easy. If cooperative games are the kiss of death, then easy co-ops are like kissing your sister in death.

This game made me think more about Arkham Horror than Elder Sign, because it's totally what I think Arkham Horror is (move around, roll dice, read cards, curse luck). It works here, and not in Arkham, because it doesn't pretend to be more than what it is. Doesn't hurt that there is much denser strategic value here (both because the dice-rolling decisions matter more here and because it's a much shorter game).

It's streamlined, but for the better. If nothing, the shorter game-time allows you to take a more leisurely pace and smell the roses with the flavor text and narrative, instead of needing to rush Arkham or having the game bog down.

Downtime in a co-op is a major downer, especially since there's nearly nothing you can do game-wise when it's not your turn. Want to play with fewer so there's less downtime and you can impact the game more, but seems like the difficulty goes even lower with fewer players because everybody gets more turns and levels up into a badass (though I guess it's easier to get killed if you have more turns). 

3+2

RATING: 1
Ha. FFG's first attempt to make 3-3.5 hour Arhkam Horror streamlined and shorter. And they managed it with a filler type game. That only takes 1.5 hours! Uhm... Yeah, kinda long for what it is. What it is, is taking Knizia's mechanism from Risk Express and meshing it with a sorta kinda adventure game. Only there's no adventure to be had, we couldn't create any atmosphere no matter how we tried, we read flavour text out loud to see if we can create some narrative, but it's impossible. Flavour text is boring, meaningless and because of bad font choice unreadable. While it's admirable how they manage to reinterpret AH's rules in a new way the result didn't really do what it was promising too. They cut too much of it. So their second attempt, Eldrich Horror was a huge success because it cut 3-3.5 hour AH to 2.5-3 hours. Whee! But they did keep the murky browny baroque and barely readable graphic design for their entire Mythos line of games.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Typical fiddly FFG chrome and bits.

Lovecraft fans will be all over this like an Ancient One over the investigators.

Players have different abilities and equipment and are racing against the clock to stop an Ancient One from destroying the earth. How? By finder Elder Signs. What's that? It's a reward you might find by completing quests. Quest themselves are yahtzee-like. Roll dice to match symbols. You have equipment that allow rerolls, locking in dice, etc.

The iOS and Android version of the game is prefect for solitaire and saves the hassle of set up. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Upon opening the box, I thought "wow this game looks cool! Wait, what's with this insert (or lack thereof)?". Oh, and that rule book--just throw it out. It's probably worded in the most complex way possible; we found a revised .pdf of the game and printed that out instead and it even incorporated a quick reference for things (which is what one would expect in a rule book!) Elder Sign is a really cool looking game, with an interesting design, but was an absolute NIGHTMARE to try to organize back into the box. Not just a nightmare--it's impossible. We had to purchase a tackle box to store all the pointless little health and sanity tokens. There seems to be a lot of unnecessary small little cardboard pieces that are a pain to store and easy to lose. We switched out the health and sanity with blue and red d10's as that was much easier than all the tokens. There's a lot of dice rolling, and considering that dice are random, there's a lot of ways in which you can change your results. There's not a lot of strategy behind the game, it's pretty light considering how complex it appears.

RATING: 6
My favorite feature of this game compared to other cooperative adventure games is the amount of variety it offers.  There are 16 different characters to choose from, each with different abilities and starting inventories.  This adds a lot of variety and replay value along with the randomly selected rooms each with different goals, rewards, and punishments for failure.

Of course with such a large selection of characters some certainly outshine others, but I personally like the imbalance.  I think a game like this should draw comments like "Yes, I got Mr. X" or "Crap, Mister Z again..."  It encourages new lines of thinking and strategies in order to win a game, that like most cooperative adventure games, isn't exactly easy.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This is the game that I had hoped Arkham Horror would be.  Elder Sign is a great co-op game for 1 to 8.  

I've never read a Lovecraft book but I know of the series and I really like the concept of this game.  The art work fantastic and the quality of the cards is great.  

I find Elder Sign to be a much more streamlined and less clunky version of Arkham Horror.  The game board is replaced by card that represent rooms in a museum. This get rid or monster movement and a couple other things. You don't gather clues in Elder Sign, you roll dice to compete tasks.  The cards for rooms have results that happen if you complete the task or fail.

I don't think of Elder Sign as Arkham Horror light, it is just better.  By better I mean, more streamlined and polished.  By no mean is any easier to win at, but it sure easier to teach others how to play.

The game is still quite the challenge and you will probably loose more than you win.  The great thing is that when we do win, it feels like a quality win and we worked to get it.  Once in awhile you'll get an easy win, the dice will just hit for you.   

I'm finding the game play and mechanics to be very solid.  Teaching others to play this has been easy thus far.  Game play can go from 20 minutes to an hour + in my experience thus far.  And I find it play solo just fine.  

This is a game I find myself wanting to play.

RATING: 6
Horrible, awful, TERRIBLE rulebook.  Game required a 6 page FAQ which changed at least 10%, if not more, of the rulebook while adding in its own share of new tweaks.

More egregiously, it didn't even fix the fundamental problem:  the game is piss-easy.  There's just no horror or interest in rolling dice to complete tasks.  Even the ones that are supposed to be difficult can usually be completed with maybe at most one failure.  I'm not sure if this was just because we rolled really well or if the Law of Averages doesn't work with this few trials, but after 5 games you would think we would have lost at least once.  The closest we ever came was 6 out of 12 Doom tokens on the Ancient One's track.  Boring...

EDIT: I finally played this again over four years later and I actually found it rather enjoyable. It was still easy, but I think I was too harsh on it back when I first rated it. Raised to a 6 for now with a pot ethical increase if I continue enjoying it.

RATING: 7
My daughter (8yo) and I had a lot of fun playing this this weekend! With her real flair for the dramatic, she loved reading all the flavor text out loud, which really did help improve the atmosphere and therefor the theme while we played.  She's looking forward to trying out some other characters now.

As far as the game goes, it is a typical co-op, which fans love to deny, but is literally just rolling dice on a spreadsheet and applying various thematic modifiers.  But therein lies the fun--all those little modifiers which play to and adjust the spreadsheet, in FFG are HIGHLY thematic.  Trust me, no one wants to see a Knizia version of these things!  Elder sign, for such a simple game, is simply rolling in theme.

The board game version is quite a bit easier than the quite difficult (played with random investigators anyway) iPad game.  There is plenty of room for both in my collection though because quite honestly, my daughter wouldn't put up with the win/loss ratio on the ipad.  plus all the tactile movement of the bits, along with the great flavor text and greater variation makes the boardgame version the real winner, even though the ipad version will do in a pinch.

RATING: 5
Mostly mindless die rolling. Fun, but too long for what it is. Something to pull out occasionally.
+co-op+

House Rules:
Speedy Signs
Investigation

* You'll need either a normal six sided die (or a few stray tokens, but I'll assume the use of a die) to track the team's Investigation score.
* When a player gains Trophies, either by completing an adventure or defeating a monster, keep the card/token as normal, but also add the trophy value to the Investigation score.
* When the Investigation score reaches 5 or more, the team automatically gains 1 Elder Sign and loses 5 investigation.
So if you had 4 Investigation and completed an adventure worth 2 trophies, you would gain 1 Elder Sign and have 1 Investigation left.
Faster Threat
* The bad new is, the threat grows much faster. When the clock strikes Midnight or 6 o'clock, add a Doom token to the Doom track.
The Museum Lobby
* When you visit the Lobby, you can take 3 actions there. Take them one at a time. You can take the same action multiple times if you want. For example, you could heal 3 sanity for free as your entire visit. Or buy 3 common items. Or visit the Lost and Found, go heal the sanity you lost for free, and then buy a common item.
* However, you CANNOT buy Elder Signs at the Lobby.
--------------------------------
Partial Binding - A Speedy Final Battle Variant
This variant is completely unconnected to the variant above. It can be used with or without it. It is less tested than the above variant, since usually the GOO doesn't wake up!
If the GOO awakens, the team loses Elder Signs equal to 1/2 the total required to Seal the GOO, rounded up. (For example, it takes 13 Elder Signs to seal Cthulhu, so you lose 6 Elder Signs if Cthulhu awakens).
If you don't have enough Elder Signs to suffer the loss, you lose immediately - your defenses are insufficient to even attempt the final battle!
If you have any Elder Signs leftover, each Sign removes 1 Doom token from the GOO before the battle begins.
However, the GOO attacks at both midnight and 6 o' clock.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I have a love/hate realtionship with this game.

Sometimes it is really great and I love it. And sometimes it is boring. 

The amount of randomness in the game make for a swingy experience. If you get easy adventure cards, no nasty midnight effects,powerful items and lucky dice throws, the game will be a breeze and boring.

On the other hand, if you get hard adventure cards, harsh mythos effects, lots of monsters, terror and at midnight effects, poor equipment and unlucky dice results, the game is frustrating and unfun. 

But when the stars align just right, it provides a tense experience, with some push you luck element. Do you go for an easy cards, at the risk of losing time before the goo awakens, or do you go for elder signs, at the risk of failing miserably. Do you keep your items for extreme situations, or do you spend them now to insure easy success. 

That is the kind of decision that this game offers.

As usual with FFG, you'll get lots of deck of cards, lots of chits, temporary effects that change from turn to turn that you have to remember applying, etc. But it's much less severe than in games such as Arkham Horror.

There are many complaints about the game being to easy. But I disagree. It just depends on many many things. Sometimes it is too easy, sometimes it is too hard, sometimes it is just fine. 

I suppose it also depends on how you play the game. If you play it as a highly strategic game, doing easy adventures to get tons of loot before tackling difficult adventures, I can see the game as too easy and unfun. But if you treat it as a push your luck game, taking risks on every turn, it is a much better game. Question is: do you play to win, or to enjoy the game?

As in Arkham Horror, I dislike the fight against the goo if he wakes up. Then it just becomes roll roll roll roll, apply goo battle effect, roll, roll, roll, roll, apply goo battle effect, until you win or you die. 

I have played with the expansion only once so not much to say about it yet.

„Znak Starszych Bogów”, czyli szybko i straszno. 

Plusy: 
1. Oprawa graficzna 
2. Solidne wykonanie 
3. Tematyka i klimat 
4. Proste zasady 
5. Mechanika 
6. Instrukcja 
7. Szybka i dynamiczna rozgrywka 
8. Świetna na wprowadzenie w świat gier planszowych 
9. Wariant solo 

Minusy: 
1. Trzeba mieć ogromnego pecha aby przegrać. Zbyt łatwa. 

„Znak Starszych Bogów” to świetna gra przygodowa. Zasady są proste a nawet intuicyjne (najważniejsze informacje są zapisane na kartach). Klimat wciąga i to, że rozgrywka nie jest długa zachęca do kolejnych wypraw do nawiedzonego muzeum. Losowość jest istotną częścią tej gry ale moim zdaniem jest świetnie zbalansowana i nie przytłacza. Mnie gra się bardzo spodobała i często do niej wracam, najczęściej solo. Jeśli chcecie pograć w coś z klimatem horroru a nie macie dużo czasu na grę to tytuł dla Was. Polecam 8/10

En el, de 1 a 8 jugadores asumen el papel de investigadores que intentan combatir a uno de los Primigenios, enormes y poderosas criaturas que habitan el espacio ínterdimensional. RATING: 7
Elder Sign is actually a remarkably fun game, though I'm aware that it has somewhat of a poor reputation. There is a lot of great atmosphere and tension here, as well as tons of different things going on at once which gives it an adventurous vibe. Yes, it can be quite easy, and yes, it's essentially a dice-rolling game, but I don't really mind this very much. My biggest con with the game is actually the fiddliness--too many small components to keep up with makes set-up and break-down quite tedious. If you're looking for strategy, this is definitely not your pick. If, however, you're just looking for some fun, Elder Sign is something you might enjoy. It's all in how you approach it.

RATING: 4
Elder Sign is a well-produced dice game that should appeal to Lovecraft fans. The designers have added their own quirk which stutters the dice-rolling a bit, but the real issue with Elder Sign is downtime.  Each player gets lots of cards to read, plenty of chits to handle, and many modifiers to pick from.  The result is fiddly and wearisome.  Elder Sign is a strong addition to the franchise, but ordinary dice lovers should try before they buy.

RATING: 9
While the setup for this one can be daunting,  Elder Sign is a fun dice roller that offers a fair bit of challenge. 

Because there are so many variables, every game is not an epic experience.  It is not due to a flaw in the game's design,  rather it is the nature of the beast in this type of game.  Speaking of the game's design,  it is well crafted and comprehensive.  Much attention was paid to detail and as a result,  the game's potential is fully realized.

As far as co-op's are concerned,  I find this an exceptional effort that,  for the most part,  gets everything right.

RATING: 7.5
Great at what it tries to do- that is condense the key mechanisms of Arkham Horror into a much quicker and streamlined game. Avoids the 'annoying leader' sydrome that co-ops can suffer from by providing enough locations and randomness that you are never sure what the best move will be. 

The theme doesn't suck you in as much as in Arkham Horror. Good story telling takes time, and Elder Sign has clearly sacrificed the story telling aspect by going for a fast experience. 

I really like it.

*Ordered from milsims August 2011.

RATING: 4
Abstract and luck-dependent. Partly because it's cooperative, it lacks narrative and room to do things that feel clever. Most of your "decisions" are really probability assessments better left to a computer.

It makes me admire a bit more the implementation of dice in Ghost Stories: There if you need an improbable die roll in order to make progress, chances are you can do something more useful with your turn than attempt that die roll.

The options in Ghost Stories' dilemmas also feel qualitatively different as their implications are usually too complicated to reduce to probability math.

My second play was comically stagnant. The situation on the board just happened to be so hopeless that three of us managed to burn through most of the 16 characters trying to get anywhere at all.

...I've been choosing to "watch" rather than play when this comes out. So dull and annoying.

RATING: 8
Elder Sign is a fast-paced, cooperative dice game of supernatural intrigue for one to eight players by Richard Launius and Kevin Wilson, the designers of Arkham Horror. Players take the roles of investigators racing against time to stave off the imminent return of the Ancient One. Armed with tools, allies, and occult knowledge, investigators must put their sanity and stamina to the test as they adventure to locate Elder Signs, the eldritch symbols used to seal away the Ancient Ones and win the game.

RATING: 9
Brilliant, tense and surprisingly dense small box game. Designed almost as 'Arkham Horror - the dice game' it actually stands up perfectly well in it own right and has plenty of unique mechanics to set it apart from its bigger relatives. Very tough to beat, and at times you will almost start to believe that dark forces are controlling the very dice themselves as you'll often find yourself just one roll short of a room victory, and will often catch yourself saying "Ackk, if only they'd rolled like that last go!" Excellent game and great value for money. Packs a lot in a small box.

RATING: 8
Beautiful, push-your-luck dice-rolling game. Played it many times and loved the cooperative component. Tends to be very atmospheric, bad things will happen and luck is a fickle lady. Quite a lot of play-throughs ended with everything hanging off the last attempt at finishing an adventure - as in - if Matej manages to solve this one and get the last Elder Sign, we have won. If he loses, the BigBad awakens and the world is lost. Even though some play-throughs were a bit on the easy side when the dice-chucking was particularly lucky (which the game easily mitigates with moving the clock faster) , it mostly ended up being quite close. The BigBad was defeated, but only half of the investigators surviving and close to death/insanity.
I had considered giving it 7/10 because I don't like that much randomness in a game, but decided to give it 8/10 just because of the wonderful art and enjoyable atmosphere of Lovecraftian Mythos.

RATING: 10
Great game!  I haven't played a game that has lead to this many cheers and groans for a long long time.  

Some complain this game is too easy and while that may or may not be true I don't hear anyone saying that it isn't fun.  That's because it is!  I for one am glad that this co-op game doesn't beat us senseless like others of it's ilk.  Arkham Horror, Witch of Salem, Ghost Stories, and Defenders of the Realm.  These games can be brutal.  I appreciate that Elder Sign is more approachable.  Each individual challenge can be difficult and that is what leads to the fun.  The designers have made a game that feels like you accomplished something without crushing your spirit.  This game will hit the table often.

RATING: 7.5
While generally our favourite games are mid to heavy weight optimizing/efficiency euros, sometimes it's just great fun to chuck a bunch of dice. And Elder Sign delivers in spades.

Gameplay is pretty simple, generally you're just choosing a room, and trying to roll the pictured dice combo. Sometimes order matters, sometimes not, monsters can come out and make things tougher, spells and items make things easier, clues allow you to re-roll dice.

One play was enough to make me ditch Arkham Horror forever. I immediately sold my entire Arkham collection, keeping only the painted minis, as they work fantastic for ES. In ES, I get all the dice rolling and decision making of Arkham, only in 60-90 minutes instead of 5 or 6 hours.

edit: Forgot to talk about the difficulty. I keep reading over and over again how easy this game is, and I keep wondering what people are smoking. In 5 games, I've had 2 massive losses (7 dead investigators), and 3 barely eeked out victories where the final seal was achieved just before the Goo woke up. And a couple of those wins are with the rules as written, allowing one card to be used as a "monster dump" when no set monster spaces are showing. With that officially changed, those 2 wins would have been sure losses, making me 1 for 5.

RATING: 7
PERMANENT PLACE IN COLLECTION

UPDATED: I love this game... But it needs a cardboard version of the iPad expansion. It's just too easy...

Probably my favourite game. I would give it a 10, but I know it's not perfect and won't suit everyone.

It's effectively a push-your-luck dice game with a Lovecraft theme. You need to match certain symbols on adventure cards by rolling dice. But good tactics are needed. You need to decide which characters to commit to which adventure depending on their equipment and special skills. For example, spells allow characters to hold back a dice that's showing the right symbol and rollover the rest. Unique and common items allow characters to roll additional dice. Some characters find it easier to commit to adventures in Other Worlds or battle monsters.

It's way too easy. We've never lost a game. But this doesn't detract from the enjoyment. It's just fun and you don't need to think too hard. A nice social fill-in game to play if you're tired.

Elder Sign is not remotely similar to Arkham Horror or an RPG. It's similar to Roll through the Ages, but with less maths.

RATING: 6
I had a quick demo game of this at Gen Con and was a bit under-whelmed. I think some rules were fudged to keep it moving, because after playing it on my own I have found it to have far more decision points than I remember seeing in that first game. It's also been very enjoyable as a solo game, as the rules are simple enough for one person to run two or three heroes at a time. 

The dice are used in a fun, Yahtzee styled manner and the push your luck aspect of taking on the more difficult missions add even more excitement. The only thing missing from the full Arkham Horror experience is the flavor text. There is a small bit on each adventure card and if you try hard enough, you can certainly piece together a narrative. Still, it's nowhere near the epic stories that play out in the parent game. Fantasy Flight dropped the ball here, because if they had just taken the time to explain what the adventurers were trying to accomplish in rolling each set of symbols, the game's narrative would have been ten times more engaging.

Elder sign won't replace Arkham Horror, but it's just about perfect when the group only has an hour or so to work with. I just hope they expand it to include more of our favorite Arkham investigators and GOO's.

UPDATE: (5/13/12)

I'm afraid I'm going to have to agree with most of the game's critics and knock down my rating a notch. Elder Sign is too easy. I'm not completely bored with it, but I do think I'm winning way too much. The spells (which are usually a big part of any Mythos based game) are dull and repetitive, not to mention they also make beating encounters way too common. Maybe I just have iOS envy, because from what I hear, the Omens version is excellent in every way. Hopefully Fantasy Flight will expand and patch the cardboard game as well. If not, I'm probably just about done with it.

UPDATE: (01/06/13)

I finally got to play the electronic version on my android phone and it has indeed been improved. The missions and monsters are more challenging and the overall difficulty level of the game has been ratcheted up. How do we convince Fantasy Flight to back load these improvements into the cardboard?

---

Meta-commentary rant added later:

The core mechanics of this game are borrowed from Knizia.  But instead of Knizia's mathematical insight and fine-tuning we have FFG's gobs of cards and bits.

I think it's depressing that the market (at least according to BGG) has clearly established that more and prettier stuff is more important than good design.  Elder Sign isn't a terrible game, but it seems ridiculous to me that this game has so many more owners and a higher rating than similar but smarter games like Ra: The Dice Game and Risk Express.

Knizia may be dry at times but he knows how to make a dice game challenging and interesting.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Elder Sign started off promising a sort of "Arkham Horror Lite". Sadly, in trimming down the game, the designers have removed most of the decision-making and excitement from it. Turns are basically reduced to: "pick a mission, try to roll matching dice". There is some limited strategy to deciding what order to attempt the missions but the choice is almost always obvious. The "co-op" element is also completely uninteresting and amounts to nothing more than "keeping" another die result. Useful but uninspiring.

I made sure to play with all updates and errata which did keep the game from being a complete push-over, yet out of 6 plays I still never lost a single game and only ever failed a handful of missions. The game is entirely too easy...the death-knell of a solo/co-op game. The lack of challenge might be forgiven if the gameplay were fun or rewarding. Unfortunately, Elder Sign quickly devolves into a bland chain of dice rolls with few stakes and no tension.

The production values are gorgeous but the visuals and Lovecraftian theme don't save it from boredom and mediocrity. Though Arkham Horror suffers from its severely demanding length-of-play, it is a far more exciting and meaningful experience. Elder Sign is certainly a far shorter affair and yet the loss of 60 minutes to Elder Sign feels far more regrettable than losing 4 hours to Arkham. Not recommended.

I do appreciate that booby prizes are given for crud luck rolling to aid future attempts.

RATING: 7
We're light/light-medium gamers, so this colour-drenched horror-fest really hits the spot. The more we play, the more we seem to enjoy. Random as hell, and fun as hell... in hell.

Once realised that spells, re-roll, focus and assist are your four best friends it does become somewhat solved, but the random nature of the dice keeps on bringing the mayhem along with the random draw of locations with risk/reward to calc each turn.

Doesn't offer the extra dice control of Nations Dice, RTTA or Ciub, but it does attract non-gamers in a way many boutique games couldn't ever hope to.

RATING: 7
The randomness of dice can make the game impossible to win, but cards and clue tokens can help overcome the randomness with rerolls and ability to change to a specific result or save a die for later. I think the mechanics are sufficient to remove enough randomness that it isn't unfun, remains challenging, and requires significantly poor luck to be rendered impossible. 

Theme is present and strong, doesn't feel arbitrary. 

Would play again.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A close cousin to Risk Express, but such a weird design: A solo experience broken into multiple player characters just so everyone has something to do.  This is only a coop game in the sense that four people in the same room are cooperating to fill their shared space with carbon dioxide as they exhale.

Pray that the game doesn't go long.  If it doesn't, though, it's OK dicey fun.

[i]Update:[/i]

Having played a second time, I'll admit my error.  Elder Sign is a good game that works just fine as a light co-op.

I'll even suggest that Elder Sign is a clear improvement over Risk Express, which has two common endgame issues: (1) players can spend their final turns doing nothing but stealing cards from each other, and (2) players can be unable to end the game because the last remaining card is too difficult to obtain.  

Elder Sign avoids both problems, which is a huge improvement.  Additionally, ES has its own thematic intricacies - monsters, spells, weapons, etc. - that flat-out make it a better game.

Both games suffer when the player number goes up, though.

RATING: 7
Great theme, lots of bits and cards and more bits and more cards.  Tons of characters.  Endless variety.  And fun dice-chucking!

Down side - the dice can just be punishing, and the game usually has a kind of inertia that means once you start losing, you're probably going to continue.  We mitigate this with a "share resources" rule that's a bit more liberal than the one in the rulebook -- this way, if one person's getting stomped by locations, the others can toss some help their way.

RATING: 8
First off, I love Co-Op and Dice Rolling Games, and this game has both... so right there is an immediate plus for this game. Not a huge fan of the Cuthulu / Lovecraft genre, but I don't dislike it either it's just ok for me. That being said this game's theme comes across very well and it's a perfect ratio between luck and strategy, which is hard to do with such a heavy dice mechanic. One negative is that it the game tends to be a little on the easy side, my friends and I and have found variants and made some house rules to make the game a little more difficult and made a good into a great game. Only other negative I would say is the price. While I love this game... it's not a $40 game. $25-$30 is probably about right for this one, but if you are a big fan of the Lovecraft theme I could see paying more as like I said above, the theme comes across very well.

RATING: 8
So, I generally end up with a huge headache when I play Arkham Horror. It's not like I play it all that often, because it takes a humongous amount of space on the table, and a load of time to place of the little bits and if you're unlucky you just end up in some corner waiting for all the other players to do their thing. 

But Elder Sign for me is my saviour. It's got the same theme (yes, I'm one of those) but it's much more slender as a game. I like the satisfaction of getting trophies as I defeat monsters and acquire locations and the suspense while wondering if we can get enough Elder Signs to defeat the monsters. It's also a cooperative game, which is something that I'm more comfortable with. 

I'd say it's got the right amount of chance and choices. Because there are different roles that you can take we'll end up deciding which locations to take depending on our abilities, even though some times the dice really have a weird sense of humour.

If I'm not in the mood for something that takes more time to set up and lasts more, this is more or less my default choice. I might also sneak it in after a longer game, if I'm not ready for bed.

RATING: 9
I love the Android application, and that is why I went and got a copy of the physical game.

I have a game group that loves dice games, and my family and some great friends love coops, and my oldest daughter and I love horror movies, so this game is a great fit for us.

I've been intrigued by the Chuthulhu mythos, but not in the RPG or any of the other board games, but this looks just right for my tastes. The various player roles also have such fun and different powers, that replay value is very high.

RATING: 7
This is a good game and was actually the first I ever purchased as a hobby board gamer. I do enjoy it, but it can be sometimes overly difficult.
