RATING: 8.5
Never have heard of this game until last Friday. That was the day, this game showed up in our house in a miraculous way. For one or the other strange reason, this game immediately attracted me. Even before the foil of the box was removed, I started reading about this game. From that moment on, I wanted to play this game badly. I almost felt sorry that we ‘had’ to go to the board-games-club in Geel yesterday. Another day that we wouldn’t be able to get this game on the table. But we knew that the day that would happen would soon be very close. First thing I did this morning, after punching all the cardboard parts, was to look if somebody did a nice job for us, by translating the game-rules into Dutch.  Well, nobody did, so I started to read the English rules a couple of times. As English isn’t my mother-language, there were some difficulties for me in the rules, but after looking some things up, in a FAQ-sheet I’ve found at the geek, everything was pretty clear to me, and I was able to explain everything to M. The game mechanics aren’t too hard to understand, so we could start pretty fast with playing. What seemed as a pretty easy task to fulfill, turned out to be a very hard job to do. Cooperation is needed in this game. By the time we discovered how we could do that the best way, M. became insane (well, her character did by losing all of it’s sanity tokens), and a new role showed up. We knew for sure, that we wouldn’t be able to collect all the needed Elder Signs. But we were lucky. The dice rolled like they should roll, the cards showed up, helped us out very well, and we barely defeated the monster.

All, I can say about this game is, exactly what I’ve expected of it, WOW! This is a whole kind of new game for us. Never played Arkham Horror before (a playing time of 4 hours is not something we like a lot), and what we have heard of the time needed to set up this game, the chance we would play it someday isn’t too big at all. First game for us of Elder Sign, took us almost two hours, but we weren’t bored for a single minute. On the contrary, within a curse and a sigh the game was at its end. This is one, which has the special spark, we’re always looking for in a game. Somebody on this world did a great (I should say: FANTASTIC) job, by picking this one out.

RATING: 9
I like Arkham Horror A LOT, but the setup time is massive, the board(s) hog(s) space and players must commit hours to play through one session.  This isn't at all a problem, because the game play makes up for these inconveniences and sometimes a long, complex game fits the bill.

Elder Sign will definitely hit my table much more often though!  Not only is the setup quick and easy, a single session is short and allows more sessions to be played in one sitting.  I very much like this aspect as the gameplay feels rewarding and each session is fulfilling.

I would go as far as saying that Elder Sign is a more streamlined variant of Arkham Horror.  Although Elder Sign is much more compact in comparison to AH, I feel that everything has more purpose, items are more useful, combat is straight-forward, and best of all, the Lovecraftian theme was not reduced. 

The artwork is very beautiful and highly thematic and almost always accompanied by flavor text which draws the players deeper into game play.  I find this aspect fun, exciting and very rewarding.  Elder Sign's gaming experience is definitely memorable!

The game components are top-notch as to be expected from Fantasy Flight Games.  Sure there do exist some minor FAQ and typos, but I am willing to overlook this since the game finds its way to the table often.

RATING: 1
Beautiful production values, as expected. I wanted to love this game. But aside from the pretty pictures and a line (maybe two, if you're lucky) of fluff text on a few of the cards, there's no atmosphere here at all. It's nothing more than an exercise in rolling (and rolling and rolling) dice  nicely clad in Arkham Horror trappings but totally failing to exude that AH atmosphere. I can safely say that this is the most unenjoyable game I've ever had the displeasure of playing - I repacked it and returned it after one play. Unless you like rolling dice over and over (and are very lucky) and figuring out statistical models so you can best plan how to approach the layout, stay far far away from this piece of junk. (BTW, anybody who says this game is too easy is not playing it right - it is extremely challenging - for example, I computed the odds of completing one of the 1-trophy adventures at somewhere around 2 in 100, even properly equipped. If you're playing it right, it's a hard game to beat. What ruins it is not the challenge level, but that it's really just about stacking the odds to beat an abstract challenge, passing or failing, going back to the entrance to re-equip, rinse and repeat as necessary. There's no joy to be had here. You find yourself more concerned with beating the odds than the Great Old One...)

RATING: 7
A cool, heavy-for-a-dice-game affair that is enjoyable and breaks the co-op mold a bit. The rules can be fiddly, but I guess being related to Arkham Horror will do that to a game. If you like intricate dice games, co-op games, or the Cthulhu mythos, you'll dig this. Be aware, however, the theme here is paper-thin compared to Arkham Horror.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Another good difficulty boost is to have every roll you make advance the clock one hour, *instead* of advancing it 3 every time. Advance 3 when at the shop.

People don't seem enthused to play this one. Not enough attachment to the characters or game narrative.

---------

Nice fun semi-light dice rolling game. But out of the box the game is too easy (unless your initial quests are all really hard). Luckily there are many different simple tweaks you can make to make it a more interesting challenge. One that sounds promising is moving the clock 5 hours each times instead of 3.

RATING: 4
Solid game, but relies far too heavily on luck. Don't misunderstand, I love luck in my games... but only to the extent that they mimic the chaotic unpredictability of real life. This is almost 95% luck, and that hampers my enjoyment.

Edit: 1/6/15
Sold it. Not worth keeping on the limited shelf space if it will never see play.

RATING: 6.5
Still undecided on the rating.

There's a fair amount of luck involved, since there's a lot of dice rolling (although it is part of the mechanics and you have options if you want to be almost guaranteed success).

Despite the fact that there's less immersion than in the bigger games it's trying to emulate (Arkham Horror and Mansions of Madness), we still ended up having a lot of fun and there were quite a few very tense moments.

Will wait to play more to give a definite rating.
